**Growth Channels**

Your tech stack should reflect where you generate demand.

 And how you convert that demand.

 These are the main B2B acquisition channels we’re thinking about:

\- E-mail outbound   
\- LinkedIn content   
\- Social media   
\- Paid ads   
\- SEO traffic   
\- Newsletter   
\- Live events   
\- Social media   
\- Communities   
\- Partnerships   
\- Affiliate systems 

And these are these are the main conversion mechanisms we’re looking at: 

\- Demos  
\- 1:1 emails  
\- Warm calls  
\- LinkedIn social selling  
\- WhatsApp  
\- Opt-in marketing sequences  
\- Automated inbound-led outbound  
\- Ad retargeting  
\- And of course, content.

But not every business is going to do every single one of these things.

In fact, many successful businesses just focus on just a few.

Which means, your tech stack should be built around your strongest channels.

And consolidate data across marketing, sales, product, and CS.

So you can build effective reports.

From evaluating over 1000+ sales tools, here are some GTM archetype tech stacks:

1️⃣ Email Maxis

\- Prospecting database: Apollo.io  
\- Scraping: Apify  
\- Data Enrichment: LeadMagic  
\- Workflow Builder: Clay  
\- Sales Engagement: Instantly.ai  
\- Newsletter: beehiiv

2️⃣ Outbound Dialers

\- Prospecting Database: Sales Nav  
\- Data Enrichment: FullEnrich  
\- Prospect Research: Clay  
\- Automated Dialer: Nooks  
\- Demand Conversion: Chili Piper  
\- Revenue Intelligence: Gong

3️⃣ SEO Hackers

\- Topic research: Semrush  
\- AI Articles: Byword  
\- Programmatic SEO: Clay  
\- Website Tracking: Hotjar | by Contentsquare  
\- Content Optimization: Surfer  
\- Visitor identification: RB2B

4️⃣ LinkedIn Social Sellers

\- Audience Builder: Sales Nav  
\- LinkedIn Signals: Common Room  
\- Content Management: Taplio  
\- CRM: Breakcold  
\- Profile Visits: Teamfluence™  
\- Outreach Automation: lemlist

5️⃣ Media Buyer

\- ABM: Clay  
\- Inbound Routing: Default  
\- AI Attribution: Hyros  
\- LinkedIn Ads Tracking: Fibbler  
\- Reporting: Supermetrics  
\- Automation: Zapier

6️⃣ Community-Led

\- Partnerships Outreach: HeyReach  
\- Affiliate Tracking: Rewardful  
\- Influencer Marketing: Favikon

#  **🎊 Discovery Questions**  

1\. What stage of growth are you at? 

* Clay Looking to refine prod5ct market fit?   
* Have found product market fit and looking to scale?   
* What is your current MRR / ARR? (100k MRR is a good ICP) 

2\. What Is your Average Deal Size (Annual)?

* 1 \- 1k  
* 1k \- 5k  
* 5k \- 10k  
* \>10k

3\. Was is your estimated total addressable market?

* 1 to 5000  
* 5001 to 10,000  
* 10001 to 50,000en  
* More than 50k

4\. Are you primarily acquiring customers through **Inbound** channels?

* Inbound Channels:   
  * Performance Marketing   
  * SEO   
  * Organic / Social Media   
  * Channel partnerships   
* How do you find the volume and quality of candidates you receive through inbound channels?  
* What is your CAC?

5\. Have you tried **Outbound** channels? 

* Outbound  
  * Cold Email  
  * Cold Calling  
* If **Yes:**   
  * What challenges did you face?  
  * How big and what was the structure of the team?   
  * What tools or platforms do you use for outbound sourcing?   
    * DIY via LinkedIn Sales Nav   
    * Database with matching algorith & power filters like Apollo/Zoominfo  
    * Manual Googling of custom sources   
  * What is your email conversion rate?   
    * The Avg. cold email reply rate is \~1% (Clearbit). And those ain't all positive.  
    *  Avg. cold call pick-up rate is \~5% depending on the industry. Apple and Android will continue making ignoring and identifying unknown callers easier.

* If **No:**  
  * What’s stopping you from experimenting?  

# **🔑 State Of Outbound in 2024**

## *Old Way*

### Why Intent / Signal-based Outbound Works 

Hyper personalise relevant messages to the sliver of your TAM that's most likely to engage based on timing and their situation. 

* **Reason:** Using different relevant data points on a company makes the personalizations in your copywriting actually provide value and context. People will read your message if it resonates with their current situation. Good personalisation that is timely and addresses real pain points will never go out of style.   
* **Outcome:** Cold email is not dead (for now). The game has changed and the winners will be those that focus on personalisation at scale. 

### Manual Research & Qualification

Sales reps spend 1/3 of their time or 10-15 hours weekly researching, qualifying and personalizing outreach

* **Main reason:** Tedious and repetitive work to manually find and organize unstructured data online.   
  * Ad hoc googling: The information is available on the web, but will be hidden in a subpage, within a case study etc.    
  * Manual lookup of tools: Need to check Builtwith, storeleads etc. On average, reps use 5+ tools.   
* **Bad Outcome 1:** Improves win rate, but lowers total activity. While simple, impossible for one rep to do at scale with 1000s of leads.   
* **Bad Outcome 2:** Spray and pray by sending thousands of unpersonalised cold emails. Inefficient low conversion that burns through TAM. Email domain reputation damaged because emails marked as spam.  

### Scaling revenue using headcount 

Hiring more reps to solve the problem is expensive and risky. 

* **Reason 1:** The average junior SDR costs about 65,000 salary \++ commission. On average, they add about 700 prospects per month to get around 25 opportunities, which really means about **$216 per meeting booked.**   
* **Reason 2:** Juniors take time to train, and have a high rate of churn when they jump to competitors to become Account Executives  
* **Reason 3:** Sales reps are not data driven and are not motivated to do prospecting work. 

##  *New Way*

### Sales Engineer / Technician

Next gen sales tools (Clay), Web scrapers powered by AI agents, and AI copywriting have changed the game. 

* **Clay:** A no code spreadsheet that connects to 50+ data integrations to let you pull any data.   
* **Webscrapers powered by AI Agents:** Autonomously performs multi-step research task on the browser. Open website \> navigate to case study page \> Find case study relevant to ecommerce  
* **AI Copywriting:** Can’t write whole emails, but can write snippets based on data pulled via Clay around relevant buyer intent signals.  
* **New Entrants To Email:** Sequencing is cheap with Smartleads.   
* **Outcome:** It doesn't take hundreds of hours of human time to prospect at scale. What used to take 30 SDRs can now be done with a single person. 

# **🪄 What SalesCraft Does**

## *Why Companies Choose Us*  

I started my agency because I saw outbound teams failing to leverage technology to optimize their cold emails. Instead of scaling with AI and sales tech, they were relying on increasing headcount. I knew I could offer a service that scales like an SDR team, but without the need for expensive headcount growth.

* Predictably increase their number of monthly sales calls  
* Scale their outbound sales without adding headcount  
* Automate (parts of) their prospecting activities  
* Partner with experts invested in their growth

**We are two things your organisation needs**

1\. A B2B data nerd  
2\. A creative sales copywriter

This first person knows every piece of sales tech like the back of their hand- they probably obsess over ColdIQ's AI tools list, they can build super advanced Clay tables, and likely have a dev background. They can write python scripts to scrape sites, can connect APIs to Clay in their sleep. This person is absolutely imperative to running good top-of-funnel motions. If you're not using the right tech, you've already lost. Having someone who can put your best ideas into action effectively is just as important as the person who comes up with them. 

The second person knows how to write copy that sells. They have a background in sales, are super familiar with effective go-to-market motions, and love experimenting with new ideas. They sit down for an hour a day and think of the most enticing offer for their campaign, they arduously pore over every word of their copy to make sure it "flows" well, and want nothing more than to pioneer a new way of selling.   
 

## *3 Areas We Focus On*  

Our goal is to provide you with a cold email system that…

1. **Set-up Your Cold Email Infrastructure**  
   1. Get better and more impressions than you would be able to get with your own process/team. This translates to emails sent and emails opened. Some teams come to us getting 7-25% open rates. Our benchmark average is 62%.  
2. **Create Segmented List of your ICP**  
   1. Target the prospects far better with waterfall data enrichment for lead scoring and qualification. This allows us to test messages in your market faster than you would be able to on your own.   
   2. Includes building company list, disqualifying, company scoring, company enrichment, contact list building, contact enrichment, contact scoring.   
3. **Messaging you are going to send that list**  
   1. Provide the expertise to take the data and create AI written personalised messages applicable to your market.   
   2. Campaign Strategy 

## *Results we aim to deliver* 

When choosing to work with SalesCraft, one of the initial questions from potential customers is often, *"What kind of meeting booking rate can we anticipate?"* To be honest, unless we draw parallels to a previous campaign we've managed, it's difficult to give an exact prediction.

We make sure your email infrastructure is (i) set up correctly and has a high delivery rate, (ii) we are emailing the right people, and (iii) all of the data scraped is accurate and used to strengthen your offer. 

After that, the biggest driver for campaign success is **how much your prospect needs your product or service.** 

Think of cold email as having a private ads network. 

* **We can guarantee impressions, with open rates being the proxy.** On average, our benchmark email open rates are 65%. If you’re getting 5-20%, you need to fix your email infrastructure, copywriting, and targeting. The positive response rate is similar to your click-through rate or conversion rate.   
* **We cannot guarantee meetings.** It is the most targeted of all channels and you have significant control, but whether people buy depends on if you solve a problem (provided we did everything right).  
* **Success for you is likely defined as no. of meetings booked…** This is ultimately dependent on how great your offer is. How much does the prospect need your product or service\! Imagine if your solution cured cancer, you can imagine how many meetings you’ll book.  
* **But that depends on your offer.** Even with excellent targeting, great deliverability, and top-notch copywriting, nothing matters unless you have a really great offer. Your offer is more important than anything else, just as it is with Instagram or LinkedIn ads.   
* **Think of how you would handle Instagram ads.** If you spend $10k with instagram and get 0 leads, you don’t go to Instagram and ask for a refund because it doesn’t work. It does work, just not for you.

Our aim is to help you experiment with cold outbound as a channel fast. If it doesn't work as a channel for your business, at least you know. We’re an agency. 3 months commitment, and then you can drop it. 

## *Onboarding Timeline*  

**Week 1:**   
“Once you sign a contract, it typically takes about two weeks to see your first campaign go live. During this initial period, we focus on setting up your email infrastructure, including creating secondary domains and mailboxes and warming them up. Simultaneously, we compile your lead lists and draft your email and/or LinkedIn sequences. This preparation phase usually lasts two weeks, allowing us to begin sending out your first outreach messages by week three.”

**Week 2:**   
Once we have prepared our initial drafts, we will send them to you for review. We will only proceed with messages that meet your approval. Additionally, before reaching out to any prospects, we will share the list of targeted contacts with you. If you are not satisfied with our targeting criteria, we will revise and adjust the lead lists accordingly.

**Week 3:**   
We provide you with a client login to our sending tool, giving you access to all relevant metrics, including: (i)The number of leads contacted, (ii) The number of emails sent, (iii) The percentage of leads who opened our emails, (iv) The percentage of positive replies. Additionally, we track further metrics like your email-to-lead ratio and contact-to-lead ratio. We also enrich these results to identify your best-performing target segments.

**Depending on the campaign, we see open rates anywhere from 50-80%.**  
**Our average leads per positive response is about 1 per 300 leads.** 

This average is backed up by a great agency run by Eric Nowoslawski (Growth Engine X) and Nick Abraham (Leadbird.io). Both send \> 1m emails each month.

**Low Daily Demand:** Cybersecurity is often sought only after a crisis or hearing about one. SEO and paid search are more effective for this need.  
**Low Priority:** Like gym memberships, people know they need cybersecurity but it's not top of mind.  
**Inbox Ineffectiveness:** Despite hacking cold email with hyper relevant messages, nothing worked.

**Number of leads For Mercu:** 

We’ve previously worked for companies reaching out to the US where it’s alot simpler to find 5000 emails per month. Globaltix. 

Data outside of the US is very sketchy, especially in Asia. I’ve run the numbers. Apollo has like 14% of all available contacts, and usually you need to divide that by 2 after validating.

Yes, the numbers go down, but I’m very confident Asia is like 4 years behind US. It’s much harder for persoanlised cold email to stand out in the US compared to Asia. If we can do good cold email at scale, it’s going to have a disproportionate impact. And I’m sure already see this with your conversion rates.

# **📬 Cold Email Infrastructure**

## *Step by Step Guide* 

**It is simple to set-up 20 inboxes.** You could do it yourself following [online guides](https://www.clay.com/blog/b2b-cold-email-deliverability). Here is a condensed step by step process that we follow internally. 

![][image3]

[https://helpcenter.smartlead.ai/en/articles/209-auto-restart-ooo-based-on-email-copy](https://helpcenter.smartlead.ai/en/articles/209-auto-restart-ooo-based-on-email-copy)  

OOO automatic response 

### Creating secondary domains 

**Why?** 

* Rotate to protect your primary domain from being burnt.   
* Bad domain reputation means your email gets blocked or sent to spam folders. You do not want your main domain to be affected.   
* Even if you send super relevant & personalised emails, a small % of people will always complain and mark it as spam. That’s how the game works.   
* Spread the attribution of spam across multiple domains to be safe. 

**How?** 

* a) Buy domains from Godaddy or Namecheap. Always buy .com or .co. Use suffixes like ‘trysalescraft.com’. Do not be too cheap.   
  * [https://www.spamhaus.org/reputation-statistics/cctlds/domains/](https://www.spamhaus.org/reputation-statistics/cctlds/domains/) Avoid these domains   
* b) Use either Google Workspace or Microsoft 365 to buy business email seats. They have the highest deliverability due to their reputation. It cost 6 USD per seat.   
* c) Here’s the math for scaling.   
  * Purchase max 3 business emails PER domain.   
  * Each email can send 40 emails per day.    
  * Generally, we start with 300 emails per day and scale as necessary. 2 domains and 6 email business emails.   
  * Downgrade to ‘business starter’ for Google.   
* Best practice is 3 domains per Google Workspace incase one workspace goes down 

### [https://help.instantly.ai/en/articles/5975326-instantly-cold-email-strategy](https://help.instantly.ai/en/articles/5975326-instantly-cold-email-strategy) 

### 

### [https://mxtoolbox.com/](https://mxtoolbox.com/)   6 Steps for configuring emails 

* Done once per domain.    
* Add a profile picture from within gmail of each account, and not from the admin console.   
  * Within admin console, search ‘profile picture’. Allow users to edit  
  * Go into each gmail inbox and upload.   
* Verification for Google of MX records   
  *  Follow initial instructions by google or go to ‘Admin Console’ \> ‘Account’ \> ‘Domains’ \> ‘Manage Domain’.   
  * Add a TXT record to Namecheap  
  * Change ‘Mail settings’ in Namecheap to Gmail  
* DKIM \- Email authentication method  
  * Go to [Admin Console](https://admin.google.com/) \> Home \> Apps \> Google workspace \> Gmail to get txt record from “Authenticate email”. Pick 2048   
  * Go to Namecheap and add it as a txt record.   
* SPF \- Email authentication technique  
  * Manually add as a TXT record in Namecheap. @, v=spf1 include:\_spf.google.com \~all  
  * Verify with this [tool](https://easydmarc.com/tools/spf-lookup)    
* Dmarc \- Email authentication protocol   
  * ​​Important: Configure DKIM and SPF before configuring DMARC. DKIM and SPF should be authenticating messages for at least 48 hours before turning on DMARC.  
  * Manually add as a TXT record in Namecheap. \_dmarc v=DMARC1;p=none;sp=none;pct=100;rua=mailto:vouch.salescraft@outlook.com;ri=86400;fo=1;  
  * Set to none, none, 100, strict, strict. Check with this [tool](https://easydmarc.com/tools/dmarc-record-generator).   
* **Domain Redirection**  
  * **Make sure people that search your secondary domain get redirected to your original domain**  
  * **In namecheap. “Domain” \> Redirect Domain**   
* Configure IMAP in email sequencer (Smartleads). Automatic google connection. Click this [link](https://admin.google.com/ac/owl/list?tab=configuredApps) in Google workspace to ‘add app’  
* Otherwise, go to gmail for each user and click on Enable IMAP in the IMAP Gmail Settings section. 

### Use [Smartleads](https://www.smartlead.ai/) or [Instantly](https://instantly.ai/) to manage inboxes

* New entrants that changed the game by charging by how many leads you have, vs traditional players Outreach / Salesloft who charged by no. of seats & inboxes. One flat rate for about $100 vs $2,000.   
* Do not use Mailchimp or Hubspot. They are designed for marketing campaigns where people have opted in for email. Hence, they use a shared / private SMTP from Sendgrid. It’s cheaper, but you’re going to get very low deliverability.   
* You can use any provider that lets you Oauth from your own domains.    

## *Deliverability Best Practices*

## 

### Benchmarking Email Deliverability 

* **Custom Tracking Domain:** Use this to track open rates. Follow this [instruction guide](https://helpcenter.smartlead.ai/en/articles/50-what-is-custom-domain-tracking-and-how-to-set-it-up-with-smartlead). Remove once you’ve verified deliverability. Any open tracking pixels make email providers more likely to flag you as promotion or spam.   
* **Bad Open rates**: Below 30-35% open rates is a red flag. There is either a technical or copywriting issue. Look for angry replies. If not, stop seeding from their domain. Create a new domain and start again.   
* **Good open rates:** Open rates are by nature heavily inflated. If your email is connected to your Apple IoS phone app, every email that comes in is recorded as opened. Use open rates to sense check, but otherwise it doesn’t matter. No one opens their email 20 times in a day\! 

### Email Warm-up Rules 

* **What is warm-up:** Free service that sends AI generated messages back and forth between friendly inboxes. Every time you send a message and it doesn’t get marked as spam, you improve your domain reputation.  
* **Specifications:** Start with 5 warm up emails for the first day of warmup, and ramp up your sending by 5 emails/day, with a cap of 50 emails/day. Set between 30-40% response rate. Don’t put it at 100%  
* **Warm-up Duration:** It takes 3 weeks to accomplish maximum deliverability. Doing 3 weeks instead of 2 improves deliverability by 30%   
* **Warm-up during campaign:** When you launch your campaign, keep the inboxes warming up, but only send 10 cold emails per day for your warm up with a 100% response rate.  
* **Starting without warm-up.** If you need to start sending campaigns ASAP, reduce your email count to 10-15 a day. Just be prepared to lose inboxes faster and have more domains ready to replace them. 


###  Copywriting Rules For Deliverability 

* **\#1 rule is to write good copy:** Compelling, personalized, and relevant messages are king. You can still land in inboxes with this, even if you have a bad technical setup.    
* **Personalise Your Emails:** Email providers can detect and will mark you as spam if you send templated cold emails that change only minor variables like first name. Use either Spintax \[\[Hey|Hi|Hello\]\]  or AI to generate lines.   
* **Use plain text only:** Email should feel like it came from a colleague.   
* **Do not use spammy words:** Words like FREE, GRAB, 50%, Jesus, Viagra, Bitcoin etc. This attracts spam filters. See this [link](https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/30684/the-ultimate-list-of-email-spam-trigger-words.aspx) for a complete list:   
* **Do not add any links:** The most common way to phish or scam via email is to make them click a link from an unknown email. Hence, email providers will mark any email with links as high risk. This includes links in your signature or an unsubscribe link.  
  * Use this instead: If this email is not relevant, just let me know and I won't email you again.   
* **Do not add images.** Images make your email heavier, and affects deliverability.   
* **Adding Images or Links At Risk:** If you strongly believe your image or link will offset any decrease in deliverability, add it to your 2nd or 3rd email. At least your first email will go through.   
* **Let Prospects Opt-out:** Either a response of ‘not interested’ that will stop the sequence, or ‘click this link’. Response is preferred to a link, but Europe and California needs links legally. 

### General Rules For Deliverability 

* **Have spare warmed-up domains:** Be prepared to lose domains for reasons outside of your control.. If you need 6 inboxes, standby 12\. Whenever 6 are active, warm-up the other 6\. Rotate each month.   
* **Turn off bad campaigns ASAP.** Eg. if you’re getting alot of complaints. Rehash copy and rehash list. Don’t pray and hope it’ll get better \- it won’t and it’ll hurt your domain.   
* **Maintain a DNC list.** Otherwise, your marked spam rate will go up.   
* **Check if you're on a blacklist.** Don’t worry about this. Most blacklist are arbitrary and privately hosted. Should not be taken seriously.  
* **Send emails consistently.** Never jump off the deep end and 3x from 50 emails to 150 emails. Send a cold email every 8-15 minutes per inbox. Otherwise, you will look like a spammer.   
* **Verify all emails before sending:** Cold emails that bounce from invalid email addresses will hurt your deliverability and domain reputation. Use Debounce or Zerobounce.  
* **Use MX matching (optional):** Send emails using the same domain as your recipient. Send from google to google. 

### Google Bulk Sender Guidelines

* The new guidelines do not apply to 5000 emails sent to Google workspace accounts. Their primary concern are personal gmail accounts.  
* If you send emails to personal Google accounts, then even if you send from Google workspace, the new rules apply.  
* For most people doing B2B cold email, this doesn’t matter to you.  
* **NEW RULE: 30 emails?** 

# **📤 Create Your Target Segment** 

**Use This [Sheet](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1OZvw998AxSF7iQH7KVI99edczeFnSNNHEDS3U_MizJA/edit?usp=sharing)**

“Segmenting a list is the most important thing. If you’re trying to sell cybersecurity solutions to a bakery, you could be Steve Jobs and no one would care.”

We’ll send you a sample of 20-30 companies to the client and keep modifying our searches until we get an 80%+ accuracy of the type of companies being targeted.

 

There are 2 layers in our process. 

##  *Layer 1:  Baseline ICP*

The minimum criteria of a viable prospect. Here’s an example for SalesCraft: 

* B2B Company  
* Inferred LTV of $5,000 or enterprise pricing   
* Less than 100 employees  
* Target personas of CEOs, Sales or marketing heads  
* Cannot be staffing/recruiting, fintech, IT outsourcing, or cybersecurity as ROI from cold email doesn’t justify the effort. 

This is our fallback Ideal Customer Profile (ICP). We will target this profile when no other data points or information about the prospect are available.

## *Layer 2: Best Case Scenario*

**We are now looking for the company/prospect that needs your solution the most\!** 

**Ask yourself this question: “If we had 10 minutes to research and qualify your dream prospect, what data points are we looking for?** 

This lets you further qualify each prospect by segmenting into situations they face that might cause them to want to buy from you.

Here’s an example of a best case scenario when looking for prospects at SalesCraft: 

* DMARC record on site is incorrect.  
* This is their first time being a founder  
* Founder(s) only have technical backgrounds  
* They have a sales rep but no Head of Sales  
* They are hiring for more sales reps  
* They recently fundraised 

**Split them up into 6-10 campaigns:** When we onboard you, we identify **6-10 personas** based on the data points. Each persona is facing a specific situation, and will get a different version of the pitch that is personalised. 

* A *first time founder* that is *technical* would get one message.   
* A *First time founder* that *has recently raised funds* and is *hiring more sales reps* would get another message.   
* *VP of sales* that is *hiring more sales reps* would get a different message.   
* Etc. 

**Think creatively, scale automatically:** List out all the possible signals that show buyer intent base on your experience. We can go on and on as long as you have a data point that you look for that would change the message.

We use AI and data tools to automatically write messages at scale. 

# **🏆 Create Your Offer**

## *What makes a great offer?* 

Rank offers by which are more like a demand capture offer vs. a demand generation offer. (Basically ask yourself "does my prospect know that this is possible today". If they all know it's possible and they know how to find people to do it, it's demand capture.). 

We want to try testing things that are **demand generation offers.** The super sexy things that your competitors can't or won't do or the things that your prospects don't even know are possible. For more info, see [this](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1nu9vasCpJ_1kKxnOw-MsHhwg89WmDlLAxUM8IbejU3Y/edit) 

**Alex Hormozi \- 4 primary drivers of Value** 

* (Yay) The Dream Outcome (Goal: Increase)  
* (Yay) Perceived Likelihood of Achievement (Goal: Increase)  
* (Boo) Perceived Time Delay Between Start and Achievement (Goal: Decrease)   
* (Boo) Perceived Effort & Sacrifice (Goal: Decrease)

**Alex Hormozi \- Enhancing The Offer With Reference To SalesCraft**

* **Scarcity:**  
  * **Why?** People want what they can’t have. People want what other people want. People want things only a select few have access to  
  * **How?** Use scarcity to decrease supply to raise prices (and indirectly increase demand through perceived exclusiveness).  
    * ***“My agency only will service twenty-five customers total. Period. We have a waitlist.”***   
* **Urgency**  
  * **Why?** Having a defined deadline or cut off for a purchase or action to occur creates urgency.  
  * **How?** Use urgency around discounts expiring to increase demand by decreasing the action threshold of a prospect.  
    * ***“I can throw in a bonus X / X% discount  if you sign the deal by Y date. Not sure how long we will be running it as we've been getting up to capacity, and this is one of the better ones we have run in awhile”**.*    
* **Bonuses**   
  * **Why?** Increase the prospect’s price-to-value gap by increasing the value delivered instead of cutting the price. Anchor the price with an initial offer, then with each increasingly valuable bonus, people feel like they’re getting more and more value. A single offer is less valuable than the same offer broken into its component parts and stacked as bonuses. It’s such a good deal it would be stupid to pass it up.  
  * **How?** Use bonuses to increase demand (and increase perceived exclusivity).  
    * ***I can throw in Bonus X (give it a name like 5 Clients in 5 Days Blueprint, and ascribe a price tag). If still not satisfied, I can stack it with Bonus Y and Z.***    
    * ***Starter \- 5,000 unique prospects a month. Bonus \- 10,000 unique prospects a month.***  
    * ***Starter \- 2 email campaigns, unlimited iterations. Bonus \- 4 email campaigns.*** 

* **Guarantees**    
  * **Why?** Reversing the risk of your product not doing what it’s supposed to do for them  is an immediate way to make any offer more attractive.  
  * **How?** If at any time they're not satisfied with the level of service you’re receiving, you can request a refund (at any time) for the program.  
    * ***Our fee structure is based on a monthly retainer. Initially, we ask for a three-month commitment to evaluate the potential success of our campaigns.***   
    * ***“Do you think I'd still be in business if I gave a crazy guarantee like that and wasn't good at what I did? Now I'm not guaranteeing you’re going to hit this goal in 3 months, after all, because I’m not in control of your offer and how it stands in the market. But I am guaranteeing that you will get $6,000 worth of value and service each month we support you. If you don't feel like we gave you that level of service, I’ll write you a check the day you tell me we suck.”***  
    * ***“Best case you get a calendar full of emails and we give you all your money towards staying with us to hit your long-term goal. Worst case you tell me I suck, I write you a check, and you get 3 months worth of free training. Both options are risk free. But, the only thing guaranteed not to help you is walking out of here today.”***

  * **Alternative Speech By Jason Fladlien**: “I’m not asking you to decide yes or no today...I'm asking you to make a fully informed decision, that is all. The only way you can make a fully informed decision is on the inside, not the outside. So you get on the inside and see if everything we say on this webinar is true and valuable to you. Then, if it is, that’s when you decide to keep it. If it’s not for you, no hard feelings. You will then, after signing up at URL be able to make a fully informed decision that this isn’t for you. But you can’t make this decision right now for the same reason you don't buy a house without first looking at the inside of it. And know this...whether it’s 29 min or 29 days from now...if you ain’t happy, I ain’t happy. For any reason whatsoever, if you want your money back you can get it because I only want to keep your money if you’re happy. All you have to do is go to support@xyz.com and tell use “gimme my money” and you got it, and in short order \- our response times to any support request average 61min over a 24/7 time period. You can only make such a guarantee when you're confident that what you have is the real deal and I'm fairly confident that when you sign up at URL you’re getting exactly what you need to BENEFIT.”

**5\. Use names to re-stimulate demand and expand awareness of my offer to my target audience.**

## *Why It’s The Most Important Thing*

Nothing is more important than your customer having a problem, and you have an offer that resonates.

New AI tools will not change this. AI tool	s are multipliers. They take what you do manually, and achieve it at scale with 1/100 the effort. 

0 x 100 is still 0\. 0 conversions without AI tools will not turn into 100 conversions with AI Tools. 

**Example: Which email did you think got more positive responses.**

Email 1: Hours spent putting together a crazy personalisation / relevancy. AI all over the place.

*hey tony, I was doing some research and it looked like a typical order on your site might be around $75 assuming someone purchased about 3 items, perhaps the attends briefs or underwear.*

*I know similarweb isn't perfect but it told me you get around 8.1k site visitors.*

*Using our internal data, I believe we would be able to help you increase monthly revenue by 1,518 \- 3037 without adding any budget to your ad spend. We do this by extracting data about your site visitors that Klaviyo doesn't have.*

*Would it be useful to hop on a call to share how we can help?*

Email 2: Put together in 10 minutes

*Hey Evelyn, we're helping brands uncover their anonymous site visitors so that you can retarget shoppers that abandon their cart and don't leave an email behind. Could I show you how it works?*

**What you can learn from the results:**

* Email 2 won \- because the value prop for email 2 was correct. Message resonated the best.  
* BUT when we took Email 2 and added the first line from email 1, we tripled response rates.  
* AI personalisation & messaging acts as a multiplier to great offers. If you get 0 responses to an offer, AI won't magically fix it. But if you have an offer that is working, AI will increase response rates when used correctly

## *How to iterate on your offer* 

A question I ask my self when creating outbound campaigns is **"how can I make this worth this person's time?"**  

There are 3 main reasons people buy products or services in a B2B setting. All of these give real tangible leverage. 

1\. Save Money \- cheaper pricing compared to competitor  
2\. Makes you more money \- investing in software that improves conversion rate   
3\. Saves you time \- Any automation tool 

There are 2 layers to iterate on your offer, and you must A/B test to experiment. 

### Layer 1: Change the value proposition 

Your product likely provides value in **more than one of these categories.** You are trying to find what the majority of your segmented list ranks as the most important reason for buying. 

Here’s an example with reference to foreign exchange sales. 

* **Save Money:** “Are you keen on exploring 0$ transfer fees compared to $120 market rates your current provider charges?”  
* **Makes you more money:** “Are you keen on exploring transfers on a 30 day credit line so you can sell more inventory?”  
* **Saves time:** “Are you keen on using our bulk transfers automation to save 3-5 hours weekly compared to manually sending 100’s of transfers?

Brainstorm & write out as many value propositions you bring to customers. \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=YIpBC_eZa34&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] Use this [Sheet](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1QxJ7gGHHW9H1CtEU_KfN_-x4pv_e0em6lJAP9yYj2yQ/edit?usp=sharing)

### Layer 2: Change the articulation of the value proposition  

There are many interesting ways you can creatively pitch the same value proposition. Here’s an example using “Makes you more money” 

*“Are you looking for an AI chatbot to improve your deal sizes in 2024?”*

No responses. Too vague. 

*“How do you know your current customer service isn’t costing you loyal customers due to slow response times?”*

2-3 leads per day. Very specific about the pain points it addresses. 

## *Lead Magnets* 

**What?** Lead magnets are described as a free offer you can make to potential customers that the market knows your competitors are charging money for. Anytime you can do what you say you can do, just show people instead of talking about it to get their attention and trust.

When you make a lead magnet, your writing will communicate the outcome you're looking to create for people in one sentence. They usually look like this. 

We help {{audience}} {{outcome}} in {{time}} {{risk reversal}}. We help teachers lose 10 pounds in under 30 days or your money back. 

It's punchy and to the point. 

**Use This [Sheet](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1Tydp9z71rS3bOdQw4HoJ_CU2XV4EAU8EjWlXXGRdQjs/edit?usp=sharing)**

### Tangible Lead Magnet. Show, Not Tell \[Important\] 

**What?** Great lead magnets are not your webinar recording, your free course, or whitepaper unless the people are willing to pay for it. It should deliver real value immediately. 

**How?**

* Identify all the problems you can address for a potential client.  
* List all the solutions you can offer to resolve those problems.  
* From these solutions, determine which ones you can provide for free and on the largest scale.

**SalesCraft Example**

* At Salescraft, if a customer hops on a call with us, we custom generate a list of 100  prospects with validated emails and phone numbers to potential customers as a free lead magnet.   
* The market (Apollo.io, Seamless, ZoomInfo, etc) gives away 50-100 leads for free. It’s obvious people think free leads are highly valued and are looking for it.   
* Our prospects know that other companies are charging real money for that and it costs us real money to provide it.   
* Data is relatively scalable for us because we have so much of it.   
* For lower effort and lower response rates, it can mean showing a completed scope of work that you did for a past client like themselves that they might find useful. Just redact the names and show them your results.   
* Thinking critically about what you can offer someone for free is probably one of the best ways to increase your response rates on campaigns.   
* It's ok, if you do things that don’t scale. Shifting your mindset from "Buy my product" to "would you meet if I could solve this problem for free?" is a better frame of thinking for a cold email”. We are always in pursuit of answering the question "if the prospect says yes, what do they get in return immediately."   
* Test lead magnets for interest before spending alot of time building them. Easier to write an email than build tech.

**Email Template:** 

I saw {{something relevant to your message}}

We help companies achieve {{results}}

But i'd never expect you to believe me without giving you something first. 

I made you a {{resource}} and I wondered if you'd let me know if it was useful and then maybe we could chat? 

**Output Email:** 

Saw you post pretty often on Linkedin. We're a team of B2B data scrapers and I made something for you. 

I scraped your past 10 posts to find everyone that engaged and I enriched them with their work emails, titles, and company names. 

Here's the link to the sheet. Just request access so I know that you got it.

**Alternative CTAs:** 

* "Could I show you the exact process we use to create this outcome"   
* "Even if we don't work together, would you want to see what's working in the market today?”   
* Could I send a list of people that just installed HubSpot?  
* If it sounds useful, we can build a list of 5,000 of your ideal customers on a call sometime  
* Let me know if you'd be interested in an audit and we can connect you with a marketer that has already grown a business in the {{industry}} space  
* We can build that workflow for free if you just send us a google sheets link.


### Intangible Lead Magnet 

**What?** For some companies especially enterprise or Software related where value is only achieved after 3 months gap and integration, you have to resort to intangible lead magnet to give something free upfront

This centers around giving away your earned insights about the market. You most likely know things about the market that your customers wish they knew and these insights are often interesting enough to entice people on a call.   
   
You can use these insights to raise the bar of your outbound email without doing a ton of free work. 

**How? 6 examples**

1\. Founding Story (eg. We know this problem very well having started 7 ecommerce brands. If you want to talk about these problems with an expert or how I sold my ecommerce brand, let's get connected)   
2\. Data we have across our customers that you don't have. What do you know about the market or industry that your customers wish they knew (I've set up all these other strategies for other companies, would you want to talk about soem of the small tweaks in your current flow that we've seen work for other people. P.S we noticed that XYZ).   
3\. Past successful customer strategies (We've worked with a marketing agency that is top 1 and work with top SaaS companies. If you book a call with me, I'll talk about all the trends we're seeing that's working well.)   
4\. Audit / Industry Benchmarking (Giving a free review of what they're currently doing. I'll let you know what's not best practice.)   
5\. Competitor Analysis (Telling you what competitors are doing)   
6\. Future Trend Analysis (What is the future, and how you should be taking steps to prepare for the future that is coming)   
 

# **❗️Three Ways Start List Building**

Eric’s Workflows:   
[https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Fw1k4SNRgxpS3je-Zw0\_4nYsRD52\_rnumjvM56zbue0/edit?usp=sharing](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Fw1k4SNRgxpS3je-Zw0_4nYsRD52_rnumjvM56zbue0/edit?usp=sharing) 

Once you’ve got your list and offer, start building your list.

* Lead databases  
* Linkedin Sales Nav  
* Custom Scraping 

## 

## 1️. *Leads Databases* 

### All rounder \- Apollo  

**Why?** Apollo has the best data across for their price point. We’ve tried Zoominfo, Seamless, Lusha, The Grid, Hunter.io etc. \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=jQGU9dbE3z4&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]. Apollo scraped Linkedin, added filters for common criteria, and enriched it with contact information. 

9/10 times, you should almost always start with Apollo if your targets are companies with good Linkedin presence. 

**How:** Creating a list of companies

* Use Apollo’s filters \[[1](https://knowledge.apollo.io/hc/en-us/articles/4412665755661-Search-Filters-Overview#01HV6V76ZGREM50QAV0QN2BZ12)\]  
  * If your ICP falls neatly into ‘*NAIC codes’* or one of the *‘Industry’* categories, start there.  
  * Segments like SaaS, Ecommerce, or general manufacturing will not fit in. Use *'Company keyword search'.* Eg. 'Manufacturing'.   
    * Apollo has done basic enrichment and tagging on whether your keyword shows up on the prospect's website.   
    * Start by checking the top 5 companies' tags. Look for more keywords to test as you add good fit companies.   
    * Only use niche keywords. ❌ software ✅ CRM  
    * Sense check effectiveness of keyword based on no. of leads in your list.   
    * *‘Exclude keywords’* to remove words like 'Coach', 'Consulting', 'Agency'.  
    * This is a poor man's lookalike search. It will not be as accurate as specialised providers like *Ocean.io* or *Owler*.   

**How:** Creating a list of contact

* Use *‘job title’* filter like 'chief marketing' or 'head marketing'. Can skip the ‘of’ as Apollo’s algorithm will automatically get chief of marketing or marketing chief etc.   
* Only export *verified emails* as it has an approx. 6% bounce rate. Do not download *unverified* as it has a 20% bounce rate  
* Use *Clay’s* integration with *debounce* to double validate emails.   
* Use *Clay* to further enrich.  
  * Company names need to be cleaned up and normalized  
  * Get emails for those without with *Prospeo, Datagma, Findyemail*    
  * Research at scale. 

**Note:** Only export these columns 

* First Name  
* Last Name  
* Title  
* Company Name  
* Email  
* Employees  
* Industry  
* Person Linkedin URL  
* Website  
* Company Linkedin URL   
* City  
* State  
* Country  
* Company State  
* Company Country  
* Company Phone

**How:** Import a list from another database to get contact information

* Providers like Crunchbase specialise in providing list of companies, but do not provide contact details.   
* *Clay’s* integration with *Apollo* has low rate limits. This means you can’t upload to Clay and enrich with Apollo.   
* Instead, download the list from your provider. Then upload into Apollo using their *‘Account CSV import’* feature. They will auto match using domain, linkedin profile etc. 

**How:** Extracting contacts for free

* Use Apollo 14 day free trial   
* Use *instant data scraper* to collect contact details names.

**How:** Organizing your Apollo account with saved list \[[1](https://youtu.be/KcUu1n-MIak?list=PLN4tvwwU-SPOfe8uoh3BXJcQ9UJPwP6xH&t=405)\]

* Save your current search as a list. It tracks all the filters you’ve used and leads you’ve identified.  Save it as 'Clientname\_Search\_date'   
* Whenever you need to find more contacts for this client, click 'exclude' list of 'Clientname \_Search\_date"   
* Then save the URL of the search WITH the exclusion of the list in your CRM. If you use this URL, it’ll always be a new fresh list you can dig from. 

### 

### Phone Waterfall

[https://www.clay.com/blog/the-best-b2b-mobile-data-providers-of-2024-with-test-results](https://www.clay.com/blog/the-best-b2b-mobile-data-providers-of-2024-with-test-results) 

[https://www.linkedin.com/posts/contactout\_3-step-workflow-to-validate-phone-numbers-activity-7139185662141927424-Bu5x/](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/contactout_3-step-workflow-to-validate-phone-numbers-activity-7139185662141927424-Bu5x/) 

[Clay](https://www.linkedin.com/company/clay-hq/) allows you to waterfall multiple mobile number providers in one table. You can use this to check multiple data providers for the same phone number as well.

Check the providers for all their numbers listed. If two come up with a repeat, odds are that's a better number than the others.

Here's the step by step process

Step 1: Build a list of LinkedIn profiles you want to find mobile numbers for

Step 2: Add whichever mobile number providers you want to use. ([Clay](https://www.linkedin.com/company/clay-hq/), Nymblr, [People Data Labs](https://www.linkedin.com/company/peopledatalabs/), and [ContactOut](https://www.linkedin.com/company/contactout/) combined are cheaper than Apollo.

Step 3: Ask AI to find the numbers from all of the providers that repeat.

You should have a much better list of mobile numbers than just trusting one data source.

This won't get the job done the same way that someone like [Phone Ready Leads®](https://www.linkedin.com/company/phone-ready-leads/) would but it can be a start for you. 

###  Email waterfall \- Prospeo, Datagma, Findymail  

| Why? | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| Due to coverage gaps, use **max three providers** in a waterfall in Clay. Each provider uses similar techniques to find & validate emails with an IP address, so more than three would be redundant. | Try Prospeo \> Findymail \> Datagma. See this [article](https://www.clay.com/blog/best-b2b-email-list-providers) for statistics. Findymail and Datagma only charge if valid emails are found, hence the most cost effective.    |

**Things of Note:** 

* **Find email from just the Linkedin:** Use Dropcontact or Contactout integration in Clay  
* **Do not send cold emails to catch-all domains.** A catch-all domain accepts all incoming email messages, regardless of whether the email address is valid. Sending cold emails to catch-all domains can result in a high rate of undelivered or bounced email. 

### Validating Emails \- Debounce  

| Why? | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| You must keep the email bounce rate below 2 to 3%, otherwise your domain will be burnt.  | Use *Debounce* ($0.0015) for best blend between pricing and quality. *Zerobounce* ($0.0064) is higher quality as market leader, but not 4x better |
| Use providers that perform syntax, domain, and SMTP checks to validate email addresses using their IP addresses for you.  | This is a commoditized service. All providers do the same thing materially \- maintain IP address reputation. They fight on price, not quality.  |

Listkit.com 

### Lookalike \- Ocean.io  

| Why? \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FGkbwUxUnOY&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] \[[2](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2Yr4KWdgjKo&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Pro:** The best lookalike audience builder. **Con:** Better than Apollo, but expensive   | Upload 3-5 best fit customers to find similar companies |
| **Use Case:** If pre-PMF, use lookalikes of your current best client for quick wins and to learn more about your value props. Namedrop case study in copywriting.  | Filter with Ocean.io *‘industry tag’* filters. Further filter using *‘keywords’* in Ocean.io native database  |
| **Examples:** Construction Rental Equipment in Singapore. Law Firms in Florida that deal with wrongful termination | By using both lookalike searches AND searches based on keywords, you can build a hard to reach TAM list. |

###  Linkedin Data \- Clay  

**Important:** LinkedIn is the number one platform to find contacts and will have the highest fidelity if found. We will always want to check first. 

**Note: Clay’s data isn’t super accurate. It doesn’t cover Asia very well. Might have to use Phantom buster to manually scrape if this is a big problem.** 

| Why? | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| Linkedin data is the source of truth. They own the data, and all other providers scrape them.  | Use *Clay*’s default company or contact search. They scrape Linkedin Sales Nav live.  |
| **Pro:** It’s free in Clay. **Con**: *Clay’s* filters are identical with sales nav which are worst than Apollo.   **Con:** Raw linkedin data is not enriched with research or contact details compared to *Apollo*.  | **Use Case:** Building company list or contact list which doesn’t need much filtering & qualification.  |
|  |  |
|  |  |

### 

### VC Backed \- Crunchbase 

| Why? | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Pros:** Specialises in VC data. More accurate and up to date than Apollo.  | Use Instant Data Scraper on pro account. Use 'exclude list' to exceed 1000 limit \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5hYHZ4UGphI&ab_channel=Ean)\].  |
| **Pros:** Comes with niche filters like (i) acquisitions, (ii) industry tags (eg. SaaS, CRM)**Cons:** No Contact Details. | **Alternative:** Apollo whitelabels Crunchbase, but is less accurate.  **Alternative:** Harmonic, but more expensive.  |
|  |  |
|  |  |

###  SMBs \- D7 Lead Finder or Outscraper 

| Why? | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Pros:** They scraped Google Maps data. SMBs may not be on Linkedin, but always on GMaps.  | **Alternative:** Outscraper, hiring on upwork, serper.dev to scrape google maps yourself.  |

###  Ecommerce \- Storeleads 

| Why? | How? |
| :---- | :---- |
| **Pros:** Market leader of ecommerce data \[[1](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/outboundphd_heres-every-step-and-every-tools-we-used-activity-7160341636684636161-Nu4o/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_desktop)\]List of info you can pull [here](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1nQ0JXQwaAqyyfBbwFan9YXXaW51hrWvvZafEpWNvaCY/edit?usp=sharing):  | Buy a Storeleads account and import to Clay with their integration.  |

### Niche Use Cases 

### 

**Cognism**: Best data for Europe. Expensive.   
**Owler**: Best for specific pre-built filters such as SaaS, Edtech, HR tech. Expensive.  
**Socialreach.com:** Best for social media data including Instagram, Facebook, etc.   
**Clutch.co:** Best for companies that are agencies.   
**Leadsift / Bambora:** Intent data. This is quite a vague concept. It could just be an intern who visited your website and Bambora classifies this as the company having interest in you. (who even knows the accuracy here)

## 3\. *Custom Scraping*

### DIY Scrape Any Directory

### 

**Why?** There are niche directories that you can’t purchase data from due to insufficient demand. Can be very valuable as they are often greenfield areas where no one else has tried prospecting. You will need to scrape it yourself. 

* Conference attendees   
* Trade fairs brochure  
* Y combinator start-up directory   
* Government websites

**When to DIY scrape?** If you are scraping 1000 webpages of the same site then, where each webpage has the same structure and format. If it gets too complex, go to upwork and post a scraping job to outsource rather than figure out yourself.  

**How?** 2 Steps To Scrape Any Website

* Step 1: Identify the structure in the URL.   
  * If there is a fixed structure, you can use Google Sheets or Clay Formulas to create a list of URLs that need to be scraped.   
    * GSheets \-  Concentenate ycombinator=5   
    * Formula \- "merge \\ "y combinator.com/companies/\\" with the first word of "/Company Name" in lowercase. If there's a second word in "/Company Name", then add a "-" and then the second word of "/Company name"  
  * If the URL has no logic behind the URL structure, you will need to use RPA.   
    * For simple pagination, Instant data scraper works.   
    * For advanced pagination, Scrapestorm is needed to mimic a human and do multiple clicks through the website to find each page.   
* Step 2: Identify the structure in the webpage  
  * You will need to map out which fields are repeating that you want to scrape  
  * You will need to map out how pagination works 

**Tool 1:** For basic scraping, use Instant Data Scraper or Clay Chrome Extension \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=twR_ENVd_d0&ab_channel=Clay)\]

* Both are free and easy to use.  
* Instant Data Scraper auto scrapes through paginations, but you will need to manually import into Clay.  
* Clay’s Chrome extension is integrated via *‘Get Data From Page’*, but cannot auto run if there’s pagination.  

**Tool 2:** For advanced scraping, use Scrapestorm

* Can overcome captcha and anti-scrape technology  
* Uses AI to automatically detect website HTML / structure, and create the scraping workflow for you.  
* Can scrape behind a log in.   
* Tutorials: \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GnRJLgcQEEE&list=PLN4tvwwU-SPOfe8uoh3BXJcQ9UJPwP6xH&index=28&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] \[[2](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=GkTKyvCXAlk&list=PLN4tvwwU-SPOfe8uoh3BXJcQ9UJPwP6xH&index=42&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] \[[3](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2iJp72iRRLE&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  

**Tool 3:** If you are scraping a popular website, check out Apify or Zenrows for an out-of-the-box scraper specialised for it. Don’t try to scrape yourself. 

* Similarweb, Indeed, Linkedin, Instagram etc. etc.  

### 

### Scrape Google Search \- Serper.dev or Clay

### 

**Why?** You can do a systematic but ad-hoc method to scrape leads if you don’t want to purchase.

**How?**  Here’s an example of for finding a list of Instagram influencers

* Site: instagram.com real estate agent AND ("@gmail.com" OR "@hotmail.com" OR "icloud.com" OR "@yahoo.com") AND ("Real estate agent" OR "Realtor" OR "Real estate broker") Singapore  
* Emails are in the Google snippet  
* Use Clay Formula ‘Extract values from data’  
* Use Claygent to identify no. of followers

[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MbgjHRHFJqM\&ab\_channel=EricNowoslawski](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=MbgjHRHFJqM&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski) 

### Scrape SMBs \- Google maps via Serper.dev or Clay  

**Why?** 7 out of 10 SMBs do not have a Linkedin presence, hence will not be picked up by Apollo. However, every SMB worth their salt will have a Google Maps pag	e. 

**How?** Clay's has a google maps integration. Do your own integration with Serper.dev’s Maps or Places API to save 400x. \[[1](https://youtu.be/8OyQrW_6gLg?si=bqehrtEQ3aGUeXo3)\] \[[15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=WFvfp45ppVY&t=1617s&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] 

* Step 1: Create a list of locations from any directory. Linkedin is a good one.    
* Step 2: For each search, enter in location (potong pasir, Singapore) and search query (eg. restaurant).   
* Step 3: Each search will return 100 results within that location  
* Step 4: Use their website to do Clay’s *‘Enrich Company’* to see if they have a Linkedin profile, even if unlikely.   
* Step 5: Use *Claygent* to to find the name of the founder/owner on the website to address the email with {{first name}}. If you already have the email, use an AI prompt to identify their first name.   
* Step 6: Use Prospeo to pull emails using Linkedin profile and first name where possible. For all blanks, run a condition to let it try finding ANY email connected with the URL.   
* Step 7: For those that are still missing emails, do a *‘scrape website’* to find as many emails like [admin@localbusiness.com](mailto:admin@localbusiness.com).   
* Step 8: Each step along the way, we validate the emails to protect the domain reputation.  
* See this Clay Table for completed workflow: [https://app.clay.com/shared-table/share\_PXSdYeyAxgwA](https://app.clay.com/shared-table/share_PXSdYeyAxgwA) 

Read this: [Patrick Spychalski on LinkedIn: Local leads campaigns have been absolutely kilning it for us (horrible… | 20 comments](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/patrick-spychalski-050649176_local-leads-campaigns-have-been-absolutely-activity-7209917841389559808-z33j?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_ios)

**AI prompt to identify first name:** 

Using the input, try to tell me what the person's first name is. The input is just an email address. Do not output a first name unless you are over 97% confident that this is their first name. If you don't know the name or are less than 97% confident, output nothing. This is the input: / Name	

# **🛠 3 Reasons We Enrich Your List** 

##  *1\. Fact check your current lead list* 

You can’t 100% trust what a company self reports their industry to be on LinkedIn, or what Apollo tells you about a company. If you have a small TAM and want 100% accuracy, enrich again to confirm. 

**Examples of common inaccuracies.**  

1\. Find if a company is B2B or B2C \- we score the company on a range of 1-10 with a custom prompt that we have. Check if they have SDRs. Check for common B2B tech like Clearbit installed on site.   
2\. Find if a company is an e-commerce store. You can’t just trust store leads or the fact they are using Shopify. Use Serper(.)dev to scrape their Google shopping listings to confirm Google allows people to buy products.   
3\. Does a company sell to enterprise companies? Scrape their pricing page for enterprise keywords and check if they have sales reps with enterprise in their title.   
4\. Check if a company has a booking link as a call to action. Use google search operators to search the site with keywords and use Serper again.   
5\. Check if a company gets a certain level of web traffic from certain age groups by scraping similar web with ZenRows   
6\. Check if a company is a SaaS company by scraping crunchbase and owler public pages for how they identify them. Again use google searches to look for common SaaS keywords like “API docs”.   
7\. If you’re targeting tech companies they almost never are categorized correctly.

## *2\. Score prospects* 

**Why?** Very few prospects will perfectly fit your best case scenario. Hence, we will pull data for each *qualification criteria* and score prospects based on how many boxes they tick and your weightage of each criteria. All accounts above a certain score will be outreached to. 

**How?** Use Clay’s very easy to use built in account scoring feature \[[1](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/outboundphd_heres-a-quick-video-on-how-to-score-your-activity-7179145392624668672-BRhh/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_desktop)\] \[[2](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nXjC6VS7YGA&list=PLN4tvwwU-SPOfe8uoh3BXJcQ9UJPwP6xH&index=17&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]

* Pick a column to score  
* Choose comparison type (eg. Contains text)  
* Input must pair with score. To make things clearer, use google sheet and create 2 columns: Criteria / score. Extract each column as a comma separated list with ChatGPT. Enter that into Clay.  
* You can check how the scoring came about by clicking into it  
* Use final **'Formula'** function**:** Add /Score and /Score and /Score.  
* Decide which prospects make the cut by drawing a line

**How to use AI to qualify at scale:** It’s much easier to use AI to figure out whether a company fits your criteria than to manually decide. For the most accurate results with GPT, score a company based on a confidence level rather than yes/no

**Example**. **Qualify By Revenue:** It's impossible for any 3rd party provider to know the revenue of private companies since it isn’t reported anywhere. They are making the best guess using algos. Better to use the employee headcount of your best clients and we'll draw a proxy from there.

* For companies above 500 employees, did not enrich revenue or funding, as they would be a good fit anyways.  
* For companies 50-250, enrich funding to see if they are above 20M.  
* For companies 250-500, enrich funding and revenue to see if they meet 100M+ Revenue or 20M+ funding. (using a condition so that it ran funding first, and then only ran revenue if no funding data was found)

## *3\. Copywriting Ammunition*

**Qualifying Criteria \= Copywriting Ammunition:** These data points make your pitch more relevant and impactful. Use it to emphasis *‘Why you, Why now’* in your copywriting. Every data point can be a trigger, if you make the connection to how your service can help the company in that situation. 

**Relevant personalisation is king:** Relevant, rather than meaningless personalization, makes your outreach more impactful and likely to result in positive responses.

* **Example:** You sell an email sequencing tool that offers fees per number of leads rather than fees per user (Smartleads).   
* **Data Found While Making Targeted list**:   
  * Identify companies using Outreach or Salesloft  
  * Understand their email volume and number of users  
  * Do they have a recently hired head of sales  
  * Have they raised funds recently   
  * Are they hiring SDRs?   
* **Data Found While Making A Great offer:**   
  * If a company sends 8,136 emails via 15 inboxes per month, do the math on how much exactly they could save by switching to your tool.   
  * Do the math on how much they could save if they 3x their team size

**Recency Personalisation as a fallback:** Recency hooks are attention hacks that make people feel like you did your research, but does not strengthen your pitch.  

* **DOES NOT** replace relevancy, a targeted list or a good offer. Only use it when there’s no available information online.   
* **Treat it like a checklist.** It just needs to make sense and can you tick it.  Recipient wants to know you put in some effort, and it sounds human so it isn't spam   
* **Example of recency**. Noticed we’re connected on Linkedin and started digging into how you help with X and thought we should connect. 

**Copywriting is based on each segment list:** Whether or not the messaging stays the same depends on how specific of a persona you end up reaching out to. You should write a different version of the email you would send manually given 10 minutes to research a prospect. 

For example, if the list ends up being a lookalike search of your current best client that has done a case study with you, we will adapt the copywriting towards that hyper specific persona. 

# **💯 3 Ways To Enrich Data**

Whatever data point you can think of, we can (probably) get. 

As a rule of thumb, we try to programmatically scrape or use 3rd party data providers. Only use AI if needed. 

## *1\. Google search \- Serper.dev* 

**Why?** Top priority\! Google has built the world's best knowledgebase. Guess what keyword an M\&A law firm will list on their website? "M\&A". We just need to execute the google search to check for it.  

* **Old way**: Sales reps traditionally do research by  manually checking whether a website has it.   
* **New way:** We do this programmatically to research at scale with APIs.     
* If you can think of it, it’s likely we can find it. Things we’ve found in the past [here](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1S95E1hOOB5V1swoJefWBhzfXDL5lX4Odlau8tAZH5jA/edit?usp=sharing).  

**How?** Creating Search Queries  

* What would I manually do if I had to research this company? Work backwards to write the query from there by eyeballing results.   
* Use boolean search operators. See this important [article](https://www.clay.com/blog/basics-of-google-search-operators)\!   
  * site: airwallex.com ("fleet" OR "construction")  
  * site:clay.com inurl:pricing "$"  
* Use Clay formula ‘*Normalize a URL’* to make the domain *bare* to be compatible with API  
* Use Clay’s integration to run the Google search on each and every lead in your list to check if those keywords exist on the website. 

![][image4]

**Notes On Using Specific Keywords** 

* You want to make sure that if they actually mention the keyword on the site, it will be on that page  
* If you are searching ‘data processing addendum’, there won’t be any page that has it except for the data processing page  
* If you’re looking at ‘pricing’ or ‘enterprise’, it can appear in so many different pages randomly. 

**How? 2 layers to executing the search**

*Layer 1: Return with the first 5 results on google, run AI on the snippet* 

**Pros:** Using the snippet as it will save on OpenAI token cost due short text length and save on scraping credits.  
**Cons:** The snippets may not have sufficient information. 

**Workflow** 

* Each search result will have:   
  * Link to website  
  * Title of website  
  * Snippet. This is created from page content and is a short preview for SEO.   
* Run AI to analyse the snippet. 

###  **Eg. Find competitors** 

* **Option 1:** Scrape the google preview text of the first 5 links with this search query: example(dot)com {{HQ Country}} competitors  
* You will likely get the G2, Gartner, and CBinsights likely. Run all 5 of the preview snippets for each of these sites through AI and prompt it to only identify competitors that are mentioned multiple times.   
* Sample Snippet: 1\. Best Airbnb alternative with a loyalty program · 2\. Booking.com: Best for stays abroad  3\. Vacasa: Best for professional management yet …  
* **Option 2:** Claygent. Downside is that it will only find one data provider. Find 3 competitors for the following company:Website. Return just the names of the competitors, separated by commas, nothing else. Example: Competitor 1, Competitor 2, Competitor 3\.   
* **AI Prompt:** Based on these company descriptions tell me why I should choose the first one over the second and complete my prefix with the main advantages. This is my prefix: """ was doing some Googling and saw /Name comes up in alternatives a lot. I could see how customers opt for you because """ . Keep your output under 20 words and never omit my prefix. This is the first company’s description: /Name. This is the description of the the second one. /Description  
* **Fewshot Prompt:** Based on these company descriptions tell me why I should choose the first one over the second and complete my prefix with the main advantages. This is my prefix: """ was doing some Googling and saw TestGorilla comes up in alternatives a lot. I could see how customers opt for you because """ . Keep your output under 20 words and never omit my prefix.

  This is the first description: Vervoe's mission is to make hiring about merit, not background.

  We help employers make hiring decisions based on how well candidates can actually do the job instead of how good they look on paper. Vervoe replaces the traditional hiring process with skills assessments and gives every candidate an opportunity to showcase their talent by doing job-related tasks. Then, Vervoe uses machine learning models to automatically rank candidates based on how well they perform.

  Over hundreds of companies have used Vervoe to hire top performers in 10% of the time. Our customers don't spend time doing résumé or phone screening. Instead, they deploy skills assessments at the top of the hiring funnel and only meet the most suitable candidates after their skills have already been validated

  This is the second description: TestGorilla works. CVs dont. Were placing people in dream jobs with talent assessments that identify the best candidates at the start of the recruitment process.

  With TestGorilla, our customers save valuable time, make hiring decisions objectively, and avoid expensive mishires.

  Our affordable tests replace subjective, incomplete, and often inflated resumes with objective, reliable, and fair results that measure aptitude, practical job skills, culture add, and motivation. Our wide-ranging, scientifically supported assessments help recruiters and HR managers to hire top talent faster, easier, and bias-free.  
* **Output:** was doing some Googling and saw TestGorilla comes up in alternatives a lot. I could see how customers opt for you because of your skills assessments and ML models. 

*Layer 2: Open up the website and return webpage content*

**Pros:** When the snippet doesn’t contain sufficient information, open up the link to the website and scrape it.   
**Cons:** Will cost more. 

### Eg. Find Pricing Of A Prospect 

* You must be able to consistently navigate to the correct page at scale. This means there’s a convention for how people show the information you need to extract.   
* Do a couple of manual googling to test.    
  * Pricing pages are easy to query. First result of site:example(dot)com pricing ""$""  
  * API page are easy to query: First result of site:airwallex.com inurl:"api" \[[1](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/patrick-spychalski-050649176_heres-a-case-i-made-in-clay-a-while-back-activity-7168251376878223360-BG10/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_desktop)\]   
* Use Clay's *'Scrape website'* integration. They've provided a pre-set list of options to collect information   
  * Title \- The title of the website  
  * Keywords \- The keywords in the metadata of the website  
  * **Description \- The description in the metadata of the website \[Important\]**  
  * Favicon \- The favicon of the website  
  * Social Links \- Links found for LinkedIn, Facebook, Twitter, TikTok, etc.  
  * Extracted Keywords \- Prevalent words or phrases extracted from the Body Text  
  * Links \- All of the links found on the website  
  * Emails \- The email addresses found on the website  
  * Phone Numbers \- Phone numbers found on the website  
  * Images \- Images found on the website  
  * **Body Text \- The body text of the website \[Important\]**  
  * Languages Detected \- Languages derived from the Body Text of the website  
* Since it comes straight from the site without any AI open-ended searching, the results are basically 99% accurate.   
* Use AI on Body Text in this case to identify their pricing.

## *2\. AI Agent Search \- Claygent*

**What?** Use Claygent to do multi step research tasks that would typically involve a person clicking through a website (eg. finding a specific type of case study on the prospect’s website). Replaces hiring a VA to manually check. 

* **Pros:** It’s replicating intelligent human work.   
* **Cons:** Claygent will always be more expensive since it's multi-step. 

**2 Use Cases**  

* **Reason 1:** The data is not always in the same place for each website. Each one of these pages are structured and look different, so you can't map it out and programmatically scrape using google search automation.  
* **Reason 2:** Many companies had ecommerce keywords without actually servicing them. We needed to do more general inference looking at the whole website on whether they served ecommerce brands. 

**How to give the AI agent instructions:** 

* Four step prompt structure  
  * Give Claygent a task to do at a high level.  
  * Give it all the data it needs to work with  
  * Explain to it how you would find the data if you were manually doing it.  
  * Give guardrails.

**Here's a list of things we have used Claygent to research for us in the past.** 

\- Finding if an ecommerce brand has a sustainability mission and what that mission is.  
\- Finding competitors of companies by checking multiple sources.  
\- Finding what the most luxury upsell a hotel had listed on the site to be able to drop in our outreach.  
\- Estimating the Average Order Value of an ecommerce store  
\- Finding reviews about products on an ecommerce store  
\- Classifying companies by sub industries by looking at their website  
\- Finding case studies listed on a site  
\- Check if a marketing agency runs reddit ads for their customers  
\- Finding company news, fundraising information etc  
\- Finding companies that mention Brands that are not on the brand website  
\- Finding how many units are under management for a property management firm.  
\- Finding when a contact has appeared in someone else's blog or podcast  
\- Taking a contact's past experience and finding company news about one of their past best jobs  
\- Finding people making complaints online about a product so the team could fix it  
\- Checking what kind of companies a VC/PE fund invests in  
\- Finding the kind of equipment/machinery a company sells so that we can make a guess on what kind of calibration services and licenses they pay for  
\- check what kind of legal services a law firm provides

And honestly so much more. I ran out of characters

**Claygent Prompts:** 

[https://app.clay.com/workspaces/305929/tables/t\_SjMTkssp8EsY/views/gv\_vDwKn8AE8tPf](https://app.clay.com/workspaces/305929/tables/t_SjMTkssp8EsY/views/gv_vDwKn8AE8tPf) 

### Eg. Find Case Studies \[[1](https://x.com/thecodycarnes/status/1782845618613784762)\] \[[2](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=DJnwrD9-i30&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  

Prompt: 

* **Step 1:** Go to website in the input and find information on up to 3 case studies that the company mentions on their website.  
* **Step 2:** The website I want you to visit is here: /Website  
* **Step 3\.** I would search on the website for any page that says something like 'customer case studies', 'case studies', 'customer success stories', 'testimonials', 'client success'. Basically, anything that gives us a page that a company would use to show that they have successfully helped other people or companies with their solution.  
* **Step 4\.** The only source that any of the case studies should come from must be the website in the input. Do not get any data from a website that is not the input. Try to do research on at least 3 case studies and output qualitative and quantitative results that the company in the case study achieved by working with the company in the input. If you can't find 3 case studies, I would rather you output alot of information about one case study than just naming other case studies. Include the problem the case study was having before they used the solution and what was their success after. Please think thoroughly through your process and take your time. It is very important that this is accurate and done well. My job is on the line that this is done correctly. If you are not at least 95% sure of the answer you are going to give, just output the word 'purple' instead as I need the answer to be accurate. If they mention case study or testimonial on the page, it's a great indicator that you found what we needed. In the output, name more than just the name of the case study. We want to know how the company actually helped the other company in the case study

**Email Line:** I saw on your site that you’ve created success for companies like {{Case Study}}

### Eg. Does this company have SOC2 Compliance?

Prompt: Help me research if a company is SOC2 compliant. Sometimes, it's written as SOC II as well.

Basically, I would google for a company website and those keywords to see if they have a page with their SOC II compliance. If that doesn't work, they usually have something mentioned on their compliance page or a privacy policy. They also sometimes put this on a security page. 

Only return results from the input website. I want to know if the input website is SOC 2 compliant

### Eg. Find people who work at target companies 

Prompt: "Using the inputs, find 3 linkedin profiles that fit the search criteria. If you have to change the job title slightly to find someone, that's fine but make sure it's a similar job title. This is the job title input /Customer Job Titles Response. These are the companies that would be a good fit /target companies response. 

I would do a google search for these types of titles and find Linkedin profiles that are good fits for these given job titles and companies. You should come back with peoople who fit the exact job titles or something very similar and someone that works for the companies that would be a good fit. The output should be the Linkedin URL to exactly 3 different people who fit the search criteria. Output the Linkedin URLs as a comma separated list with space after each comma. Don't add any additional information in the output. 

It is important that you only output a link directly to a personal Linkedin profile that fit the search criteria. make sure to filter your information by job titles and company the person work for. These are the only relevant metrics. Make sure the job title always fits: /job title"

**AI Prompt: Find me customer reviews of my prospect** 

Find me the reviews of the company on either google or yelp. I want to find a review of a happy customer. This is the website /website Bring me back what the customer said and their first name as well""

**AI Prompt: Find me the webpage of their most popular product in their ecommerce site**

Two step Claygent workflow. 1\. to find out what is the most popular product of the target company. 2\. Find the product page for that product. 

## *3\. Clay’s Integrated Data Providers* 

Clay has done the heavy lifting by integrating with every possible data provider you might need. My job is to apply best practices and pull the data for you. 

For everything not plug and play, check Zenrows or Apify first. Otherwise, you can use Clay’s HTTPS API to integrate any API yourself. 

Two providers require some explanation: Zenrows and Apify. You can easily feed the data to Clay with the integration, but you will need to navigate scraping via their platform.  

### Linkedin Company Enrichment With Clay

**Why?** It gives you so much information about the company.   
**How?** You will need either the Company Linkedin URL or Website Domain. 

* Use Linkedin URL for the best accuracy.   
  * It comes with Apollo by default  
  * Pull the URL from the '*Enrich person from profile'* integration's latest experience on their profile  
  * Use *Google Search* via Clay using company name & Linkedin for accuracy  
* You can pull from website domain, but will be less accurate  
* If you don't have the domain or Linkedin URL, use the Clearbit integration to get the Website Domain for free from just the company name \[[2](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3FLCx6L3e1o&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\].   
  * Usually used after scraping a directory and you don't have website links.   
  * If Clearbit doesn’t work, use Claygent or Google: "Find the Linkedin page of the /Brand on Linkedin"

### Apify 

**Why?** Apify is a marketplace of custom scraping tools. Similar to Zenrows, but different business model. Use it for what Zenrows can't do. Facebook, LinkedIn, TikTok ad library scraping \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=e6Oh_SDzLXM&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]

Watch this:   
[https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cil5\_ZQs-Fc\&ab\_channel=BrandonCharleson](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=cil5_ZQs-Fc&ab_channel=BrandonCharleson) 

**How to guide:** 

* **Step 1: Create Task**  
  * A task in Apify is a predefined configuration for running an actor. It allows you to set default input values, making it easier to run actors without specifying inputs every time.   
* **Step 2: Define Inputs**
