  * Inputs are the parameters you provide to an actor or task to customize its execution. These can include URLs to scrape, search queries, or other configuration settings.  
* 

**Firecrawl.dev**  
   
Scraping multiple pages of a website indiscriminately

### Zenrows 

**Why?** For cheaper data at scale, scrape it yourself with Zenrows rather than buy from a provider**.** Cost about .0001 \- .0025 per datapoint depending on how much anti scrape the pages have. \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=RRSAEih3pDw&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]

All these platforms have publicly available information that you can scrape without being logged in.

* **Builtwith**: scrape public builtwith links for technologies. Every public builtwith link is builtwith(.com)/detailed/{{domain}}  
* **G2 & Capterra:** scrape for reviews and data  
* **Owler:** scrape for funding and competitor data. site:owler.com "{{company\_domain}}"   
* **Glassdoor:** scrape for jobs, reviews, and company information  
* **Indeed:** scrape for job information  
* **Crunchbase:** scrape for company data like total funding, funding rounds, events attended and sponsored, investors, M\&A activity, etc.   
* **Similarweb:** scrape for web traffic details  
* **YouTube, Gartner, Comparably, Clutch**, and other pages

**Step 1:** Use Serper to find and target the page you need to scrape.

Serper helps you get access to it programmatically. So if you want to scrape Owler you can find the page you need by searching. site:owler.com "{{company\_domain}}"

This will return results with the website on the page.

**Step 2:** Point the page that you found with Serper to the scraper in ZenRows. Use the functions in Clay to format and verify the data 

#### **Eg. Qualify By Revenue** 

Alternative: Use a series of Google Searches to ping the Crunchbase, Apollo, zoominfo, and Glassdoor programmatic pages to find the estimated revenue from these sources. Use AI to blend all of the results together.

Upload a list of domains you want to research to your trusty Clay table. Connect Serper.dev to your API so you can save Clay credits. 

Create google searches to find Owler, Crunchbase, and ZoomInfo public pages 

Site:crunchbase.com “{{targetdomaincom}}” revenue  
Site:ZoomInfo.com “{{targetdomaincom}}” revenue  
Site:owler.com “{{targetdomaincom}}” revenue

What you’ll get is in what is called the Google Snippet, a bunch of revenue numbers. Ask AI to analyze the snippets and average together the revenues for your own revenue number based on the best providers. Or you can cut to the chase and just do a google search for ZoomInfo’s revenue number

#### **Eg. Classify B2B vs B2C company with AI:** 

**Step 1:** Use a confidence level, rather than yes /no based on description

Evaluate if this company is a business that sells to other businesses or if they sell directly to consumers. If you are 100% confident that the business is B2B output a 10\. If you are 100% confident the business sells to consumers, output a 1\. An example of a company that would be a 5 is a company like Facebook who does most of their marketing to consumers but makes all of their money from other businesses. An example of a 1 is a company like an e-commerce brand that sells products to gym goers. An example of a 10 is a company that consults other companies on how to grow.

**Step 2:** Check if a company is a SaaS company by scraping crunchbase and owler public pages for how they identify them. 

# **📛 Applying AI To Data Points**  

* **AI is not a silver bullet.** \[[1](https://www.clay.com/blog/ai-sales-prospecting#if-you-need-convincing-to-use-ai-for-sales-emails-read-this)\].   
  * It’s just a tool that helps you scale, not a copywriting strategy.   
  * Always think about what you would say as a human to another human. Write it out manually. Then think about how that can be done at scale with AI.  
* It **CANNOT** write cold emails entirely for you. In these cases, the AI often “hallucinates” lines or ends up sounding overly sales-y— because of the copy that it has been trained on.  
* It **CAN** write snippets of copywriting. Create an email template with static and variable sections {{custom variables}}. Use AI to personalise the variable sections.   
* Use Clay's email drafting feature can be used for previewing and sense checking while writing

### Prompting Basics

**4 parts to your prompt \[[1](https://www.clay.com/blog/ai-sales-prospecting#2-basic-ai-sales-prospecting-prompts%20")\]**

* **Part 1:** Generally instruct AI on what you want it to do.   
  * Start by clearly stating what you want to accomplish with the AI. This just helps AI get it's direction going and is the part I think about the least. For example, ""I want to write a sentence about the mission of this company in under 15 words.""  
* **Part 2:** Provide Reference Data  
  * The biggest mistake people make is simply pasting a website URL or a company name and asking AI to write about it. That is a sure fire way to give AI the opportunity to hallucinate complete non sense for you.   
  * Instead, give it specific data to reference so you know that the information it is making decisions off of is correct (or at least you only have your self to blame if things go wrong.)  
* **Part 3:** Refine Your Instructions and constrain it's creativity.   
  * Be precise about what you want. Specify the word count, keywords to include, and the tone or style. This is where you have to remember you are talking to the world's smartest person and they have 0 context on what you need.   
  * For example:, ""Keep the output under 15 words, use keywords from the input, and write in simple language.""    
* **Part 4:** Give Examples of what you want the output to look like  
  * Show examples that match the desired output format and style. Clay has built in **fewshot prompting** so this is easy. This helps AI understand the structure you’re aiming for. 1 to 2 are usually fine.   
  * From here, I edit the prompt based on what I see. If the output is too long, I edit part 3 to make it shorter. If it's speaking with language that no one would use I say to speak at 5th grade reading level and don't be overly complimentary.   
* **Final tip:** I've legitimately found an increase in my prompt accuracy when I add a little bit of a guilt trip. Like so: ""Keep in mind, I really need you to get this right, otherwise, I might get fired. Take your time and don't just output the first thing you think of. Think critically about what I'm asking you to do and output text that meets all of my criteria. I am counting on you to get this right."

### Fewshot Prompting Example

**Original prompt:** Using the input, craft a sentence using my parameters. Begin each sentence with this phrase """ I know you're busy helping  """ and add a 5 to 8 word phrase after it that summarizes what this company does. You'll know what the company does based on the input here which is a description of the company: """/description.  """. Complete each sentence with this phrase """ and bookkeeping is probably not at the top of your list. """ Follow the rules for my output. 

**Example 1:**   
**Input:** Using the input, craft a sentence using my parameters. Begin each sentence with this phrase """ I know you're busy helping  """ and add a 5 to 8 word phrase after it that summarizes what this company does. You'll know what the company does based on the input here which is a description of the company: """ We started 1620 to make the best workwear in the category. To give hard-working skilled laborers the product they have been looking for and deserve. For years we watched our family and friends working in outdated cotton canvas gear that didnt fit and functioned poorly on the job. Cheap products that actually caused fatigue and made their lives harder. By using best in class fabrics, patterns, and making all our products in the USA, 1620 has reinvented workwear. """. Complete each sentence with this phrase """ and bookkeeping is probably not at the top of your list. """ Follow the rules for my output.   
**Output:** I know you're busy helping workers feel comfortable in high quality workwear and bookkeeping is probably not at the top of your list.  

**Example 2:**   
**Input:** Using the input, craft a sentence using my parameters. Begin each sentence with this phrase """ I know you're busy helping  """ and add a 5 to 8 word phrase after it that summarizes what this company does. You'll know what the company does based on the input here which is a description of the company: """ Mohinders is a small shoe business based in San Francisco, Mumbai, and Athani, India. We're a small-but-mighty team of four: 2 in San Francisco; 1 in Amsterdam and 1 in Mumbai. Our designs are deeply rooted in the shoemaking traditions of Northern Karnataka, a region in India. We work with families of 3rd-and 4th-generation shoemakers and leather tanners. We strive to uphold respectful design and sustainability from start-to-finish. This means heirloom, regional processes, intentional choices to reduce waste and use lower-impact materials, and creating shoes that last and age beautifully. We work with ten different groups of master shoemakers, all cooperative members based in Athani. Most are families who come from generations of master shoemakers, and work in neighboring workshops near a shared cooperative office and meeting space.

Learn more about us over on our website and follow us on Instagram @mohindersshoes\! """. Complete each sentence with this phrase """ and bookkeeping is probably not at the top of your list. """ Follow the rules for my output.    
**Output:** I know you're busy helping design traditional Indian shoes and bookkeeping is probably not at the top of your list. 

### Cost Estimates Using AI 

Open AI costs \~7 cents per line

* Prospect's website scraped programtically rather than with AI for content using Clay  
* Text summarized with GPT-3.5 to avoid using GPT-4 tokens  
* GPT-4 used to write messaging

#  **📣 3 Types Of Data And How We Apply AI** 

There is a non-exhaustive list of *data* we can identify at scale about your prospect that we can use as ammunition to do highly relevant copywriting. 

**To recap, ask yourself this question: “what would you say to your ICP if you had 10 minutes to research them manually and write a customer message?"** 

**"If you could let the SDR who knows your business and your customer the best repeat a task everyday, what top things would you want them to do?** 

**We will find out which tool you need to get it done.** 

**Connect the dots: Find data points unique to each prospect, and get creative about how you use it to sell. Every data point can be a trigger, if you make the connection to how your service can help the company in that situation.** 

**Uniqueness: The best outcome is a message so personalised to each target that if you showed it to another random company, it would not make any sense.** 

**Here’s an example of what I did for Airwallex, a cross-border payment company.** 

You could use Clay to figure out the different countries people have employees in, and use AI to figure out what the currency is of those countries. Then mention you noticed on Linkedin you have a person in India, and a person in China, and a person in France. 

Are you doing salary payments in Rupees, Yuan and Eur manually with a bank? Typically we notice…. 

We usually test multiple angles and stack them in one single campaign. Watch [this](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=XdXzpsMJhkI&t=25s&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski) or [this](https://clayrun.notion.site/4-Our-13-best-AI-prompt-templates-7c8ded9fcd28417bbcee123e15440134) 

## 1️. *General Company Background* 

### Company’s Competitor 

**Email Line:** I was doing research and {{source}} told me that people often compare you to {competitor}

### 

### Company's Sub-Industry

**Why?** Shows you did your research, and can show you focus on their niche market   
**How:** Extract company description from *‘enrich companies’* in Clay. Run AI on it.   
**AI Prompt:** Based on the company description I provide, tell me what industry the company resides in. Be very specific and limit output to less than 4 words. This is the company description: /description 

### 

### Company's Mission / Summary 

**Why?** Shows you did your research, and can tailor a unique solution for them. One of the most useful. We saw almost double response rates from prospective clients  
**How:** Extract company description from *‘enrich companies’* in Clay. Run AI on it.   
**AI Prompt \- What they do well:** "Using this company description, tell me one thing that 'company' likely does very well for their customers. Format your answer as an action \- for example, if the company is good at building sandcastles, say ""building sandcastles"". Keep the output under 4 words. Here's the description: Description. "  
**AI Prompt \- Summary:** Using the input, generate a sentence summarizing what a company does. This is the input: ""{{Company Description}}"". Keep the output under 8 words and use specific keywords from the input. Complete the sentence with my prefix. This is my prefix: ""I was on your site and saw you…”"  
**Email Line:** I saw how you helped people {{mission of what they do}} and wanted to reach out  
**Email Line:** I saw on the site that you've created success for companies like {{case study}}.

**Sample Email:**

Jeanne \- I was on your site and it looks like you help empower women through innovative, transformative programs.

The reason I’m reaching out is because we help expert based businesses scale their marketing efforts.

For example, we’ve helped Brian Tracy International, an expert led business, just like yours, grow their online sales from $1,200/mo to over $200k/mo.

We have a framework that our clients take advantage of to repeatedly scale their business.

When’s a good time to walk through them?

**AI Prompt for Sample:** AI Prompt \- Mission: Using the input, summarize the company mission in one sentence. This is the input: “{{Company Description}}”. Keep the output under 12 words and use keywords from the input. Complete each output with my prefix. This is my prefix: “I was on your site and it looks like you help”

### Job Titles Company Sells To

**Why?** Shows you did your research, and can tailor a unique solution based on the prospect’s niche customer focus.   
**How:** Extract company description from *‘enrich companies’* in Clay. Run AI on it.   
**AI Prompt:** Determine the job title or type of customer that this company usually sells to, using the input as a guide for what they do. The input is this: /description. Who gets the most value out of their product and what is their usual job title? Give me up to 3 job titles of types of customers. Do not include any numbers or extra information. Just a comma separated list of titles or types of customers. It is a list of 3 titles so it should be formatted with and in between title 2 and 3 to be gramatically correct. Example: CEOs, Startup founders, and CMOs. 

### Generate Potential Target Companies For Prospect 

**Why?** Shows you did your research, and deliver upfront value to them.   
**How:** Use GPT integration, but time limited. Use Claygent, but it will cost more. If you want greater diversity, run it twice and tell GPT to exclude any of the companies that came out of the first input.   
**AI Prompt:** Using the input, output a list of 10 companies that would be good targets for the company from the input. This is the input: /description. Truly think deeply about what the company from the input does and a company that would be a good fit for them to sell to. Try to name companies that also are a good fit by company headcount. Not everyone wants to sell to Tesla. Be niche and think thoroughly about companies that they can sell to. Don't just output fortune 500 companies. Give me a list of 10 companies that are comma separated.

### Use Analogy To Paint A Comparison

**Why?** Analogies help people visualise your solution, especially when you compare it with what the prospect does best. Eg. The same way you guys help people save money on fashion, we help companies save money by scaling outbound without hiring people.  
**How?** Pull some data points via Clay integrations, and thene run a GPT prompt.   
**AI Prompt:** Using the input, create an analogy connecting how the company in the input helps their customers and how we can help them. The description of the company that we are looking to create an analogy with is this: /Description. The analogy should be specific and relate to how our company helps our customers. This is how our company helps our customers. ""we help people automate their Sales outreach using automated cold email systems, 40 data providers, and creative copywriting sequences in order to increase sales without having to increase headcount."" Most of the time, companies help people save time, save money, or make more money. First think of how the company most obviously helps another company or customer and then analogize that to how we help customers. Make the output just one sentence that's under 20 words. "  
**Email Line:** A good way to think about us is the same way you help people {{how they help}}, we help {{how you help}}.

### Send 3 Creative Ideas Of How Prospect Can Use Your Product: 

**Why?** Share innovative ways someone can leverage your product or service in their business. Gets 1 in 100 positive reply rate. 

**AI Prompt:**   
I'm going to give you a description of /Company name. Then, I'm going to give you a description of my software caled Clay and it's capabilities. Output a list of 3 bullet points outlining ways in which /firstname, a /jobtitle at that company, can use Clay to improve processes within /company name with Clay.Output the bullet points, nothing else. The bullet points should be no more than 15 words long each. Reference /normalisedcompanyname at some point in the output.  
/Company name Description: /Description  
Description of what Clay does.  
Give long paragraph

**Sample Email:** 

Hi X,

It looks like \[Company Name\] helps manage and protect Microsoft infrastructure. Have you considered running any of the following outbound campaigns to gain new customers?

\- Target IT managers involved in cloud migration, offering tailored solutions to simplify their transition  
\- Reach out to CISO or security managers, highlighting your security and compliance benefits  
\- Email Microsoft certified professionals, emphasizing your compatibility with Microsoft environments and how you can increase their efficiency.

Are you doing any of these right now, or would you need to help automating or initiating any of them?  
\*\*\*\*

**Sample AI Prompt:**   
Using the input, create three bullet points of creative outbound marketing ideas for a company. The ideas have to be possible with cold email marketing. This is the input: \[company description\]. Analyze who their target audience would be by job title and think of creative ways to market to them. Be specific and give unique advice. Keep each bullet under 15 words and use strategies that use outbound marketing.

**Email Line:** Specifically, I think it could help you {{AI generated line about how this company could use it based on what the company does and the prospect’s role}}

Very popular line\! 

### Relevant Keywords On Website 

**Why?** Scrape websites for words or synonyms that represent an ICP. \[[10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=kpmMVdm0DKA&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  
**How?** Pull the data from the Google Search and use '*Find Keywords*',

* Extract Company description, SEO description, and Keywords from Clay enrichments  
* Merge via a formula into a new column.  
* Run Clay's "Find Keywords" feeding it the new column, and then identify if keywords exist  
* Create 2 outputs.   
  * No. of keywords found.   
  * Which keywords were found 

**Alternative:** Directly use Clay’s '*Find keywords in website'*   
**Email Line:** I notice on your site you mentioned {{keyword}} on this page: {{Insert Link}}

## 2\. *Intent Signals Based On Company’s Current Situation (subject to change every 3 months)* 

###  Problems they might face today

**Why?** Shows you did research, and pokes the bear at what challenges they may be facing. The more I learn about your company, the more I think we can help.   
**How?** Pull some data points via Clay integrations, and then run a GPT prompt.   
**AI Prompt:** Here are a few stats about /Company name. Stat 1\. Stat 2\. I run a company called SalesCraft that does lead generation. Use the stats to craft a creative pitch to use in an email marketing campaign. It should call out a problem with their scores and suggest a way to improve them. It should be a snippet, and only 2-3 sentences long. Don't write an entire email, nor include the subject line. Leave out quotation marks of any kind. Just proivde the insight, not a pitch  
**Email Line:** "As I learn more about your company and how you help democratise access to software development talent"

### Identify recent news

**Why?** Did something good or bad happen that indicates the prospect might be keen. Otherwise, just used as a recency hook to show you did some research.   
**How? ** Use *PredictLeads ‘recent news’* integration. Run AI on *'article title'* to save on AI tokens, even though using the article body would be better. 90 days ago is a good time frame.  
**AI Prompt:** "Using the input, complete my prompt using keywords specific to the news article. Compliment them on the findings of the article. Keep it very short and casual. Make sure to leave out corporate jargon. Shorten company names when applicable. Don't make any references to the time of the article being published. The input is /title.   
**AI Prompt:** Using the input, summarize a recent news article in one sentence. This is the input: {{News Article Headline}}”. Keep the output under 12 words and use keywords from the input. Complete each output with my prefix. This is my prefix: “I saw the recent article about”  
**Email Line:** Saw the recent news about {ai summary}

### Recent Fundraise or Launch 

**Why?** Strong signal they will need to grow.   
**How?** Use this as a filter, don’t mention that they recently raised money as it’s overused. \[[21](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-Ue3S-NdX8o&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  
**Example of first line:** I figured customers might reach out for support around things like utilizing the new AI Writer tool in their s fales process.

### Open Jobs

**Why?** Identify current challenges the company is looking to solve through job postings. Also, use this to indicate growth intent. \[[3](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mqeY94YEB78&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]

**Different Ways To Find Job Posts**

* Use PredictLeads, waterfall into Google jobs. Google jobs will be messy.    
* Use Clay’s *‘Find Job Post’* integration that scrapes Linkedin, the no.1 white collar job site.   
  * This will be more backdated. If it needs to be real time, DIY with Phantom Buster.   
* Use Apify to scrape Indeed, the no.1 for blue collar jobs.   
* Apollo also has a job opening filter, but there's a drawback. If you look for a job posting, it only shows the first 10, and they don't tell you what job posting is. Good for quick & dirty, although inaccurate.   
   

**AI prompt:** Use Open Jobs To Identify Quality Of Candidates The Company Is Hiring For (Staffing & Recruiting Context).   
"Using the input, create an inference about what it would take in order for a person to be successful in the role. This is the job description /Job Opening. Consider the most important quality the applicant must possess in order to fulfill this job. Then quote in the job description where you made that inference from. Output the inference in a sentence that is under 20 words, and looks like this. """"I saw that in order for the Commercial Sales Manager to be successful, you need someone who is on time because the description said that ""this person must be punctual. """"  When creating your inference do not use the same words as what is in the job description to make the quote so it looks human. Follow my format in the example everytime.” 

^ Use two AI prompts, instead of one.  

**AI prompt:** Infer Company Needs from Open Jobs (Example 1\)  
"Tell me what the problem this company is trying to solve based on the open job that is listed in the input. Keep it short and be specific based on what that job title is known to be tasked with in a company. The input is 'title'. Complete this prompt: I saw your company was hiring for 'title'. In my experience, this means you're trying to improve the company's "

**AI prompt:** Infer Company Needs from Open Jobs (Example 2\)  
"Using the input, infer why a company is hiring for the role. The input that I will give you is the company description and the job title they are hiring for. This the company description input: “ {{Company Description}}”. This is the job title input: “{{Job Title}}”. Take your time to think about what the mission of the company is and how hiring this role would help them accomplish their mission. When completing the output, generate text about how hiring this role would solve a problem. Complete the output with my prefix. This is my prefix: “I saw you on your website that you are hiring for a {{Job Role}}. In my experience, companies hire for this role to”"

**Email Line:** Noticed you're hiring for a {title} and the job description mentioned {keyword}  
**Email Line:** Noticed you're hiring for a {title} and it looked like this person would be responsible for {responsibility} considering the job description said {actual quote from the job description}   
**Email Line:** Noticed you're hiring for as Customer Support Associate. Took a look at the job description and it looked like they will need to respond to emails with appropriate answers to customers. Are you thinking about how AI can be leveraged to speed up this process?

### Recent New Hire / Leadership Change

**Why?** Target new hires who may be looking to make impactful changes in their new roles.  
**How?** Utilize Clay’s ‘Enrich Person’ data to identify who has less than 2 months work experience on Linkedin \[[2](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=3FLCx6L3e1o&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  
Double check tho to make sure they’re not an advisor.   
**Alternative:** I saw this person just left your company, don't you want to replace this person? \[[1](https://youtu.be/EJxyp1cX6pI?list=PLN4tvwwU-SPOfe8uoh3BXJcQ9UJPwP6xH&t=830)\]  
**Email Line:** Noticed you've been the {title} for about {time} years and figured you were the right person to reach out to.  
**Email Line:** Noticed you recently took over as {title}  
**Email Line:** I noticed on Linkedin that {new leader hired} recently joined the team and I'm sure they have a lot of new goals for your team\!

### Employee Headcount Growth 

**Why?** Target companies showing growth through increased employee headcount. This is a very good form of traction metric that acts as a proxy.   
**How?** Utilize Clay’s *‘Find Company Headcount Growth’* to pull this data from Linkedin. Note that % growth here refers to the last 1 year duration, not the last 3 months. This is via Linkedin customer support. \[[5](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JOQ68jqTutg&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]   

**Example of first line:** I noticed that 6sense added 20 customer support people in the last 3 months. Are your current processes still working with the team growth?

### Department Headcount Growth 

**Why?** More specific to the team that is growing. Department headcount growth is even more specific if you’re targeting a specific team.   
**How?** Utilize Clay’s *‘Find Employee Headcount By Criteria.* You can filter by months and you run two columns

Minimum number of years that they person has been working \- 3 months (Old)   
Minimum no. \- 0 months (current)

John \- 0 months  
David \- 2 months  
Tim \- 3 months   
**Seth \- 5 months**   
**Alay \- 12 months** 

### 

### Companies With No Dedicated Team Members for Task 

**Why? 2 likely scenarios**

* If the company is small but growing, they’re likely facing more challenges you can help with. Eg. you could reach out about how the tax deadline is coming up and if they need help with their books leading up to April 15, you could help.   
* If the company is large or has been around for \> 5 years, this means the company is very likely outsourcing the function. Send your best lead magnet/message for why you are better. 

**How?** Use Clay's *‘Find employee headcount by job title’.* If answer is 0, likely they'll be outsourcing.   
**Alternative:** Apollo’s filter for employee headcount is not as accurate as Clay. Clay is laser accurate and the source of truth because it pulls direct from Linkedin with little delay.  This tutorial \[[16](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ZwdQJJ3YZHM&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  
**Example of first line:** Noticed you aren't using any support tech on the site. I'd imagine that since the business was founded in 2014 and you just broke 100 employees that your old processes might not be working any more. 

**Sample:** 

**Email 1:** 

Kelly \-- I was on your LinkedIn and noticed you have kept the team pretty lean.

Have you thought about bringing on a person to take care of repetitive tasks like assisting in scheduling consultations with clients, streamlining communication with event partners, managing social media promotion for planned events.

The reason I ask is because we help business owners offload tasks to virtual staff so that they can stay focused on the higher leverage, more rewarding elements in the business.

Would this be worth a chat?

**Email 2:** 

Kelly – to add some context, I figured you might have parts of your business like designing breathtaking event themes and decor that you find rewarding, and other tasks (like the ones I mentioned in my previous email) that can feel downright draining.

Would it be useful to outsource some of the less rewarding tasks to virtual assistant (VA) staff for a fraction of what US employees would cost?

**2 Part AI Prompt for sample :** 

* Prompt 1: Using the input, give me three ideas for a small business on how they could use a virtual assistant to help them. This is the input: {company description}. Keep the output under 15 words per idea and be sure to output the ideas in one line separated by a comma. Be creative and use keywords from the input.  
* Prompt 2: Using the input, create a 6 word output with some of the most rewarding tasks within a business. This is the input: {company description}. Keep the output under 6 words. Keep the output in all lower case and be specific about the task. Complete each output with my prefix. This is my prefix: "to add some context, I figured you might have parts of your business like”

### Technology Used 

**How?** Use builtwith. Clay has integrated with it, and they are the best provider who has been in the game for the longest since 2007\. Has the database with the most amount of websites and technologies built up. \[[8](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-4yiioErNyk&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] Apollo whitelabels Builtwith. Can use Apollo's filter although it won’t be as precise.   
**Limitations 1:** Builtwith is limited to technologies installed on website. If you're looking for technology like Salesloft or Wise, Builtwith won't work.  
**Limitation 2:** It detects software that people have already uninstalled. Caveat your line with ‘history of using tech’.   
**Alternative Solution:** Use Predictleads ‘Find tech stack’  integration which identifies technology by scraping open job descriptions. Otherwise, manually scrape job descriptions and run an AI query.  
**AI Prompt:** "I run an organic marketing agency. I'm going to give you a list of technologies that /Name, a prospective client, uses. Give me the one most relevant to improving SEO performance, in the form of the first line of an email to that prospect.  For example, if they use google search console, say ""I see you use google search console \- glad to see you're taking initiative with indexing your website. Don't use any subject lines or quotation marks. Here is the list of technologies: /technologies  
**Email Line:** I used the BuiltWith chrome extension on your site and noticed you had a history of using {{tech}}  

### Identify Which Competitor They Use

**Why?** Messaging can directly identify a competitor's weaknesses. Have different things to say depending on which competitor they are using.   
**How?** Use Builtwith technographic data or Predictleads \[[17](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-4yiioErNyk&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]   
**Example of first line:** Noticed you're using Zoho Support, have you found their multichannel inbox to be useful in support or are things falling through the cracks?

### Identify Which Complementary Tech That You Integrate With

**Why?** Leverage a partnership model or a good relationship with another provider.   
**How?** Use Builtwith technographic data or Predictleads \[[18](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=-4yiioErNyk&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] 

### 

### Find website traffic

**Why?** Look for climbing growth in the last 3 months as a strong indicator. However, this is a proxy. No provider has cracked perfectly accurate web traffic data so caveat it. You can also identify which countries they sell to.  
**How?** Use SEMRUSH clay integration for quick and dirty. Zenrows scraper for Similarweb will be cheaper at scale. Use a Clay formula to pull the data out since Zenrow doesn't parse it.   
**Email Line:** I know similarweb isn't perfect but they said you had around {{number}} visitors per month 

### Social Media or Reviews Page

[**https://thewebscrapingguy.com/**](https://thewebscrapingguy.com/) 

**Why?** Their follower count or activity levels can be very good proxies. For marketing agencies, you may want to use AI to give suggestions on how to improve it. 

**How?** 3 ways to do it (Ranked) 

* Use Clay's 'Scrape website' to find the Instagram listed on the website  
* Use Claygent for searching with AI  
* Use Clay's Instagram integration for searching without AI  
* But note yelp/google review is done for you in Clay.   
* Can try https://dataforseo.com/

This is also the order I would waterfall the providers in as well. Scrape website comes straight from the site and is basically 99% accurate. Claygent is doing some searching with AI. Instagram integration is searching without AI.

**Email Line:** Noticed on Google Maps the 4.8 star reviews you all have  
**Email Line:** Noticed on Yelp, the review {{person name}} left about {AI summary of review}

###  Prospect Is Running Ads

**Why?** Check if leads are running ads and adjust messaging accordingly. Check if leads are running ads and compare with competitors. Target companies running ads with specific keywords. Target companies running specific types of ads and suggest transformation opportunities

**Email Line:** Noticed you're bidding on keywords like {{insert keywords}}  
**Email Line:** I saw your ad about {{Insert ad summary}}

**How? Instagram & Facebook Ads** 

* Get list of leads from Storeleads   
* Download CSV of instagram URLs, and then upload into Apify to run the actor.   
* Go back to Clay, and automatically pull the scraper that has run in your Apify, and load the table into Clay.   
* Lookup Record in Other Table (Clay 2.0) \[[1](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/patrick-spychalski-050649176_i-created-an-email-flow-that-references-a-activity-7178745101832060928-QLt7/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_desktop)\]   
* [https://www.facebook.com/ads/library/?active\_status=active\&ad\_type=all\&country=AU\&media\_type=all\&search\_type=page\&view\_all\_page\_id=946272522105063](https://www.facebook.com/ads/library/?active_status=active&ad_type=all&country=AU&media_type=all&search_type=page&view_all_page_id=946272522105063) 

**How? Linkedin Ads** 

* Linkedin just changed their ad library so you can filter by keywords mentioned in the ad and by companies.  
* Head to LinkedIn Ad library, create searches. URL structure for each search is standard. The URL can be broken down with custom variables in each place.   
  * ads by Secureframe in UK mentioning "security" in last 30 days \= [linkedin.com/ad-library/search?accountOwner=Secureframe\&keyword=security\&countries=GB\&dateOption=last-30-days](http://linkedin.com/ad-library/search?accountOwner=Secureframe&keyword=security&countries=GB&dateOption=last-30-days)  
  * /ad-library/search?accountOwner={{company   
  * }}\&keyword={{keyword}}\&countries={{country}}\&dateOption={{date option}}    
* Tip: for country code and date, I get those straight from the ad library search result. For the company name, in my testing, the slug of the company url on LinkedIn gets the best accuracy.   
* Create a spreadsheet so you can create these links in bulk. Have a sheet with your target accounts. Ask Chatgpt to write a google sheet formula that replaces the variables with the company name in your sheet.   
* Go to Clay to have **Claygent** access the page or use **Apify** to scrape the pages in bulk. The Apify output will include all the information about the ad and can always be imported to Clay for further enrichment. 

   
**How? Google Ads**

* Use Clay's Google search tool to access a company's Google ads.   
* Use the 'Include Ads?' feature. This is a feature of Google Serper that you can toggle.   
* Use AI to generate what keywords they’ll likely be running ads for.   
* Experiment with multiple search queries. 

### Find Ranking on Google Organic 

**Why?**: For marketing agencies trying to sell SEO.   
**How?**: Use AI to find what keywords that a person would search for if they’re looking to buy from company’s service. High intent and ready to buy keywords. Google search this: “Csv imports” or “done for you csv imports”, then use ‘filter list of objects’ and find a keyword that is the client’s domain.  

**Email Line:** I did a search for {{relevant keyword}} and saw you were ranked {{Rank}}. {{Comment that changes based on their rank. Compliment them if it’s high, suggest improvement if it’s low}}. 

### Average Order Value For Ecommerce Brands 

**How:** Watch this \[[1](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Hlc4dMZDF7s&t=1s&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  
**Email Line:** I was looking at your site and it looked like the average order is about {{Value}} considering if someone purchased {{items}}.

## 3️. *Decision Maker’s Background* 

### Decision-Maker’s Last Job

**Why?** Good personalisation since you can assume people left their past job to work on exciting new problems. Most likely, they didn't join to do the boring stuff you help them solve. E*g. I'd have to imagine you didn't leave {{past company}} stoked to worry about {{problem}}*   
**How?** Use Clay's *'Enrich Person From Profile'* that gets all info from their Linkedin profile, including all their past work experiences.   
**Email line:** ""Hey Suchita, noticed you recently were promoted to Principal Customer Success Manager in March. Before working at 6sense, I saw you worked at Yext. Noticed both companies are using Zendesk and Drift right now. How's your experience with them?""  
**Email line:** I figured you didn't leave {{previous company}} stoked to worry about {{boring problem you solve}}

### Focus of their current job

**Why?** Shows you understand and empathise with the challenges the decision-maker faces.   
**How?** Use their job title and descriptive summary of what the company does, and then run on GPT.   
**AI Prompt:** Tell me what is the focus of this person's role based on the title name and the input. The title name is /Job Title, the input is /Summary. Complete this prompt with the tasks they are responsible for in under 5 words. As the 'job title', i'd imagine you focus on "  
**2 Part AI prompt:** 

* Prompt 1:  Using the input, write out 2-3 problems a person is responsible for solving in their role. This is the input: “{{Job Title}}”. Be specific about the particular problems a person in this role faces that a person in a more generalized role would not face. Keep the output to 2-4 sentences and be very specific about the problems they face.  
* Prompt 2: This is the input: “{{Summary from last AI prompt}}”. Considering these problems and responsibilities, pick out what problem my company solves that would resonate most with this person. These are the problems my company solves: “{{Insert your value propositions}}”. Complete the output with my prefix. This is my prefix: “When I speak to other {{titles}}, they tell me they see problems like”

**Email line:** I figured you were the right person to reach out to considering {{AI generation of an explaination based on their linkedin profile}}  
**Email Line:** "Hey Seth, I know you're focused on growing the social presence of SalesCraft and you probably hate thinking about expense reports." 

### Linkedin Post By Decision-Maker

**Why?** You can use the content of the post, especially if it’s related to the product you sell.    
**How?** Use Clay's *'Find recent posts by user or company'.* This is Linkedin. Set it to about 20 days ago  
**AI Prompt:** Using the input, complete a sentence summarizing what someone's last LinkedIn post was about. This is the input: \*\*\[Insert Post\].\*\* Keep the output under 12 words and use specific keywords from the input. Complete each output with my prefix and do not incude quotations or hashtags (\#) in the output. This is my prefix: "I saw your recent LinkedIn post about"  
**Email Line:** Saw your linkedin post about {{summary of what their post was about}}

### Used to Work at Your Client and Moved to New Jobs: 

**Why?** Leverage existing relationships by targeting former employees now in new roles. \[[10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eYRrqi6Fmn4&t=1s&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]  
**How?** This tutorial \[[10](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=eYRrqi6Fmn4&t=1s&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]

### Never Held The Position Before

**Why?** Individuals who just got promoted into a senior role they’ve never done before are more open to new solutions.  
**How?** This tutorial \[[15](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=a6yNcpL514I&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\] Find experience in ‘enrich person’, and then ***‘filter list of objects’***   
**AI Prompt:** Using the input, summarize the LinkedIn profile in a couple of sentences. The input I will give you is in JSON format. Here is the input: “{{Input a whole LinkedIn profile}}”. Summarize the profile for me and look out for specific parts about their profile. Besides giving me a general summary, also tell me: 1\. Has the person held their current role multiple times or is the first time they are in this seniority?  2\. What is their current role’s focus? 3\. Do they move jobs often? For all of this data look at their LinkedIn profile and think methodically before answering. Summarize the output in 4-6 sentences focusing on what I want to know about them.  
**Email Line:** I did some research on Linkedin and it looked like this is the first role you've been a {title} before. Kudos

### Identify Decision-maker’s colleagues

**Why?** Use it to check if you’re talking to the correct stakeholder and ask for a referral. 

**How?** Use Clay \[[1](https://youtu.be/KR9MMEycuIk?t=185)\]  

* Use Clay’s *‘Find Contacts’* integration via Linkedin once you have the company.  
* Make it a separate department that is adjacent to your primary department. eg. if you were searching for HR managers, switch to Engineering heads.  
* Exclude the title of your prospect so we DON'T call out their name in the email (Use Clay's Job Title Exclude Keywords)   
* We use AI to clean the person's name so that we don't ask a referral to Josh Smith CPA, MBA  
* One more *'find keywords'* search using the current decision-makers’ name to safeguard against causing a blunder of asking a referral to the same person we are reaching out to.   
* A formula column outputs the clean name OR "someone else" as a fallback in case we can’t find anyone. 

**Email Output:** Best Used In Breakup Email 

"Hey {{First Name}} \-- 

Is {{Other person with similar role at company}} the right person, given they lead {{department or role type}}?

I know there’s about {{Rounded employee headcount number}} employees over at {{Company Name Cleaned}}. Perhaps this isn’t in your purview.  

### Call Out Recommendation 

**Why?:** Use as a P.s line to show personalisation.   
**How:** Clay’s Linkedin integration comes with it.  
Saw the recommendation name {{recommender name}} left about how you {{Summary of what the recommendation said}}. Kudos\! 

# **🎯 Sales Frameworks & Strategy**

There are many reasons for why your prospect should care about your product or service. 

We use your *Offer* and the *Data Points* to creatively brainstorm copywriting angles and then A/B tests to find out which works best. 

Most outbound copywriting are (i) making an offer, (ii) communicating an outcome, (iii) asking if you have a problem, or (iv) trying to give something valuable for free. 

We take the time to fit your *Offer* and *Data points* into any of the following copywriting frameworks depending on context. 

## *Specific Problem Identification*

**What?** Find a data point that indicates your prospect might be facing a problem you can solve. If the person indeed has that problem, check if they would like help fixing that problem. 

Staffing and recruiting offers are perfect examples of this. They check if someone has a problem with hiring qualified people, and show that they can help fill roles with some example resumes.

**How?**  Ask a question intended at making the person think differently about the problem. Either something they havn't considered, or it's a big fat problem. 

We scrape online reviews, forums, and social media for keywords where users are complaining about slow response times or unresolved support tickets. We can gather these complaints, compile a report, and approach the SaaS company's leadership, showcasing how our customer service enhancement platform can help reduce response times and improve ticket resolution rates, leading to higher customer satisfaction and retention.

"I saw on G2 a customer was wishing there were CSV import improvements in the product""

Instead of asking “do you need help with automating sales commissions”, ask “how do you keep track of varying sales commission rates for each role and their accelerators”. 

Classic example: Instead of saying how are you preparing for your ironman? Instead say how are you training so that you don't get shin splints weeks before the big race. 

## *Use AI to help your prospect visualise how your solution helps their business*

**What?** We train our AI model to understand your offerings and how they benefit users. Then, we use AI to give ideas about how a product or service would directly apply to a person's role given their role, our value description, and the prospect company description. 

**How?** This works when your solution has multiple use cases. For instance, take clay.com. One user might leverage the platform to craft outbound campaigns targeting startup founders, while another could utilize it to enhance their inbound leads.

""Wouldn't it be useful if a manufacturing company with 200 employees saw different messaging on your site than if a publishing company with 50 employees came to your site?""

## *Do the math*

**What?** Pull data points, and infer how much $$ they’ll save/earn, or time they’ll save

**How?** Hey we're checking company analytics, and saw you had this many visitors per month. Based on that, we think you could convert this many more customers monthly if you improve your site speed by 1 sec, assuming conversion rate is about 2.5%. We optimise your entire website significantly increasing speed.  Can I send you a quick video showing what's causing the site speed issue? 

## 

## *Perfect Timing Window*

**What?** This is when you only reach out when 5-10+ data points in the best case scenario are true. Your client is clearly in a buying window that you can help (eg. hiring, fundraising, employee just left, new product launch etc.) 

Alternatively, wait to reach out when the perfect trigger arises. 

**How?** This would take a list of around 200k CEOs and refine it so you are only reaching out to the 10-20k that are most likely to need you right now instead of messaging everyone broadly.

Target: Venture backed Start-ups   
Solution: We help you fundraise 

We would take the total TAM, and pull data points every month to see who qualifies. 

## *Social Proof Via Lookalike Clients* 

**What?** Leverage the social proof you have of your best customers to target more companies within that niche. Your message now becomes "we've been there done that with a company just like you, want us to show you how we did it?"

**When to name drop:** If the case study is known to the prospect and is similar to their company, it can boost reply rates and add credibility by referencing a real, verifiable company.

**When not to name drop:** If the prospect is unfamiliar with the case study company or it's not similar, it can decrease the outreach's relevance.

**Decision Criteria:** Match the case study to company size/industry and split test mentioning the company name versus just discussing the results to determine what works best for each client.

**Example:** This would segment the travel industry to find outbound travel agencies that encounter issues with large one off payments to China. As the industry is small, you can generate FOMO since each brand recognises the other.

Target: Travel Agencies  
Solution: We help you with cross border payments. 

## *Solve a small problem upfront*

**What?** Give immediate upfront value to your prospect. Send them messaging pointing out something a brand ought to know about their customers. 

**How?** Hey, we ran a quick analysis of your website and found that your load time is over 3 seconds. Is that something you’re aware of? Might affect your user experience.

If they reply, respond with an open conversation and take it from there. If not, next email can be a normal pitch.  

Target: Ecommerce brands   
Solution: Optimise website performance 

## *Flex expertise*

**What?** Be straight to the point, and show you have the expert know-how. Go deep about how your process works. If you have a competitive advantage underneath the hood, use that to your advantage. 

**How?** Reflect on the unique elements, founding story, or secret sauce features of your product or service that could have a transformative impact on your prospect.

Close with a no-brainer offer that the prospect must be stupid to say no to. 

**Example:** 

"Hey {{First name}} \- {{relevant first line or fall back line}} 

We started {{your company name}} becasue {{tell a little bit about your founding story}} Today, we've helped companies like {{case study}} achieve {{result}}. If we could help you do the same, would that be useful? "

## *Deal with objections upfront*

**What?** If you know your customer well enough and their common objections, deal with the elephant in the room before someone even brings it up. 

# **💌 Writing Cold Email**	

## *Copywriting Best Practices*

### Basics

* Keep email under 100 words.  
* Avoid spam words.  
* Clearly state the reason for reaching out.  
* Use simple language (5th grade level).  
* Focus on the recipient, not the sender.  
* Include social proof with quantitative results.

### Personalizing

Think backwards from what you would send with 10 minutes of research and think about how you can automate that. 

### 

### Subject Lines

Do not come across as a sales email. 

* “Don't Sign Your Next Marketing Contract Until You Do This"  
* "The Last Project Management Tool You'll Ever Need"

Stick to the tried and tested defaults

* First\_name \<\> Your Company    
* Quick Question, First name   
* First name \<\> sender first name

Experiment with 2-3 words that is something a colleague or customer might send to them. Eg. Outbound Plan for 2024\. 

### Email preview text

Preview text length is about 90 characters. You should put your persoanlized copywriting that shows you’ve done your research to stand out here. 

### Call To Action 

**Aim for a reply, not a click or a meeting:** A call to action where ‘if this is interesting, book a meeting on my calendly’ is bad. 

* “If it's interesting, worth a chat? OR if I could solve this problem, worth a chat?’ will 5x your reply rate. Only sales folks do book a meeting so it will seem very salesy. 

**Strong existing offer or lead magnet:** If you have a solution to a hair on fire problem you’ve identified, feel free to ask for a call straight away. If not, go ‘softer’ and just aim to get a reply. “Would this be interesting to you”. 

**Be very specific about value:** Explicitly state how you’re going to make it worth the prospect’s time. 

* Show clear value that will be given to the prospect in exchange for them taking the next step. Think: "how do we sell them on taking a meeting vs. selling them on our entire solution?"  
* "Would you want to hop on a call about this?" vs "If we could cut customer support response times in half within a week, would you be interested in a short call?

## 

### Email Sequence Length 

* **4 emails is standard**   
* **Large TAM (over 50k prospects):** we keep the sequences short as you can easily use that sending capacity for fresh prospects.   
* **Small TAM:** We may increase the number of emails. However, no more than 5 emails as unsubscribes go through the roof. You can assume spam reports are following the same trend.  

### Maximizing Your TAM

* **Purpose:** Avoid burning through your list too quickly.   
* **A/B test copywriting with small batches:** We start by running A/B test on value propositions and your offer with about 200-400  prospects per cohort. Only scale once you’ve done enough testing to know what the best possible copywriting is   
* **2-3 months before re-reachout:** You can always reach out again. No one remembers that they ignored a cold email, but you must wait long enough so that you have fresh *buyer intent signals* to build the copywriting around.   
* **How we recycle the list:** Once the list is finished, we start re-reachouts right back at the top again.  
  * Use fresh data for buyer intent signals as the prospect’s priorities will have changed 60 days later. This will keep the emails relevant.   
  * Revamp the messaging based on what we learnt the first time going through the list.  
  * It’s more work, but we have reused a list now 4 times and it still gets leads every day.    
* **Breaking it down with an example**  
  * We start by asking what the lead generation target is. For instance, 10 meetings per month. It takes about 300 leads to get one positive response, so we need to reach out to approximately 3,000 leads to secure those 10 meetings.  
  * If someone’s Total Addressable Market (TAM) includes 9,000 people, we would distribute our email volume to contact 3,000 leads per month (including follow-up emails). This approach ensures we don’t exhaust the list too quickly.  
  * We then start again. Redo targeting and copywriting with learned insights. 

##  *Standard Sequence Structure*

* 4 emails. First email introduces a fresh idea, and the second email adds on to it with extra context.   
* New subject line makes it look like a fresh email 

**Email 1:** New email thread  
**Email 2:** Same thread as email 1   
**Email 3:** New thread.  
**Email 4:** Same thread as email 3\. 

### Email 1 

The purpose of Email 1 is to introduce our offer to the prospect. We want to come armed with the homework we used to research them and explain why we are reaching out and then most importantly, explain why this email is worth their time to engage.

---

Hey {{first\_name}} – 

{{recency waterfall OR relevance based first line}}

Specifically, I think it could help you {{AI generated line about how this company could use it based on what the company does and the prospect’s role}}

If we could help you {{messaging to be tested}}, would that be useful to you?

Signature

P.S. {{custom AI generated call out}}

---

**Let’s break it down**

{{recency waterfall or relevance based first line}}  
	

* *Recency \= foolproof. Eg. Noticed your post about XYZ, started digging into how you help with X and thought we should connect.*   
* *Relevance \= better, but may not always be present. Eg. Noticed on Linkedin that XYZ joined your sales team recently.*

Specifically, I think it could help you {{AI generated line about how this company could use it based on what the company does and the prospect's role}}

* *Rotate and A/B test between different key value propositions. Eg. We help B2B SaaS companies scale their outbound without increasing headcount.*  
* *We leverage AI to train a model on your offerings to your customers. We then input information about the prospect's company, allowing the reader to visualise how your solution can benefit them in practical terms based on their context.*   
* *This is the key line. We manually write 10-20 to make sure we nail this line.*

If we could help you {{messaging to be tested}}, would that be useful to you? 

* *Ask yourself “How do we make this worth this person’s time”*  
* *This is where you can insert one sentence about your offer or lead magnet.*   
* *Testing multiple variations of your offer is necessary to find what your audience resonates with.* 

Signature 

P.S {{AI generated analogy}}

* *Analogy is based on one of 3 concepts prospects care about: saving time, saving money, or making more money. The same way you guys help people save money on fashion, we help companies save money by scaling outbound without hiring people.*

### Email 2

The purpose of Email 2 is to give more context on how we can assist and what it means for their business or personally, building on top of email 1\. 

It looks like you handle {{responsibility}} so {{company}} can keep helping people {{mission}}, but let me know if I should speak to someone else. 

* *Shows you did your homework on the decision-maker and the company*

{{explain in more depth how we made the value prop in email 1 possible}} 

* *Add things you cut from email 1 due to word count.*  

No need to hop on a call, could I send a video of how it works? 

* *If they didn't respond to our initial message about scheduling a meeting, offer a lower hanging fruit so it’s easier for them to bite and reply.* 

Signature    
 

### Email 3

By this point, we've sent two emails without hearing back. It’s similar to email 1, but we want to switch things up in two ways.  

* We need to change up to a different value proposition.  
* Lower friction by changing your CTA 

{{First\_name}} – {{often for this first line, we use something similar to email 1 and do another line about why we are reaching out now.}}

{{Switch value proposition so it’s different from email 1}}.

{{New Social proof around a different value proposition}}

{{CTA that is lower friction for the prospect to respond to}}. 

### Email 4

Email 4 is the break-up email. It signals to the prospect that this is their last chance to reply. It creates urgency in case the prospect is interested, but too busy to pick it up now. 

Let me know if {{full name of employee 1}} or {{full name of employee 2}} would be better to speak about this.

* It’s possible that you’re speaking to the wrong decision-maker. Use this to get a referral.   
* It shows you did your research. 

I had 3 ideas about how we could specifically help over at {{company name}} 

{{Idea 1 generated by AI}}   
{{Idea 2 generated by AI}}   
{{Idea 3 generated by AI}} 

* Help connect the dots for your prospect by clearly painting what you can do for them 

Do any of these look like a fit that we could discuss with your team?

## *Sample Email Sequences*

## 

### SalesCraft Email Outbound Sequence

Subject Line: Outbound Plan for 2024

**Email 1:** 

Hi {{First Name}, 

**I was on your site and it looks like you help {{AI summary of company mission}}.**

{{recency waterfall or relevance based first line}}

7. ***Given {{Full Name of SDR}}’s role as {{SDR/BDR}} on your team, I had to assume you’re using outbound strategies.***  
8. ***Noticed you recently took over as {title} in {month}. In our experience, this means experimenting with cold outreach tactics to see what works best.***   
9. ***Given you’re hiring for the role of {title} and JD mentioned {quote}, I had to assume you are using cold outreach tactics.***   
10. ***With an {{enterprise}} price point, I had to assume you are using cold outreach tactics as it looks like you’re B2B selling to {{job titles}}.***   
11. ***From what I could tell on your Linkedin profile, noticed you are a first time founder with a technical background working at {{company}} and {{Company}}. Had to assume you’re using cold outreach tactics to find customers.***  
12. ***~~I had to assume you are using cold outreach tactics to compete with {{top competitors}} that came up in Google as an alternative alot.**~~*

I started my agency after helping scale two hyper growth VC backed tech companies with outbound automations. 

Are you exploring how you could leverage data scraping and GPT-4 for prospecting? 

***1\. We've helped B2B companies send up to 5000 personalised emails monthly without hiring more headcount.***   
*2\. We help B2B companies scale their outbound without adding headcount.*   
*3\. If so, would it be worth taking some time to show you how we can automate persona and account research for your outbound team?"*

I can demonstrate on a call by building a list of 100 of your best prospects with emails for free. Want to make that happen? 

**Email 2:** 

"{{First Name}} – 

I did more research on {{Company}} and came up with 3 cold outreach tactics that could help with growth: 

{{Creative Ideas}}

\- Identify financial institutions posting about customer loyalty or NPS on social media and engage.  
\- Reach out to banks with recent customer complaints online to offer solutions for improved customer experience.  
\- Target fintech firms that recently raised funding to offer personalized financial solutions to their customers.

Have you solved for automatically creating and qualifying customer lists or is your team still doing data enrichment manually? 

If we could help you do the same and save 7+ hours a week, would that be useful?

Best,

If this is not relevant to you, let me know here. \[[1](https://www.linkedin.com/posts/outboundphd_this-is-quite-possibly-the-craziest-clay-activity-7140701920247066625-1hfM/?utm_source=share&utm_medium=member_desktop)\]

**Email 3:**

*‘Considering your CMO role and you’re in charge of marketing and so you can help fitness enthusiast breathe better’*

### Clay’s Outbound Sequence

Clay's outbound message, But GEX uses it for his own agency \[[1](https://youtu.be/Vtsa9hfXEHc?t=638)\] \[[2](https://clayrun.notion.site/6-How-Clay-Uses-AI-within-Clay-e47210d5544141f6ad811605d7654f49)\] \[[3](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=ILKYwZ60EeA&ab_channel=EricNowoslawski)\]

**Email 1:** 

"{{First Name}} – I was on your site and it looks like you sell to {{job titles}} titles. It looked like you are helping {{AI summary of company mission}}.

I had to assume you are using outbound tactics considering {{Full Name of SDR}} is an {{SDR/BDR}} on the team.

Are you thinking about how they could be leveraging better data and GPT-4 to do their prospecting?

The reason I ask is because we are helping companies like Rippling and Ramp with our tool that collects the data and writes the messaging for them.

Would this be worth a chat to build a custom outbound table for you?"

**Email 2:** 

"{{First Name}} – as you’re helping people {{AI summary of company mission}}}, I’d imagine you are using outbound marketing tactics like the following.

{{Creative Ideas}}

Have you cracked how to do this persona targeting and data enrichment automatically or is your team still using tools like Sales Nav to do manual research?

If so, would it be worth taking some time to show you how we can automate persona and account research for your outbound team?"

**Email 3:** 

{{First Name}} – I sent an email a while back with the subject “Outbound edge” that probably didn’t do a good enough job showing you how we could help your outbound team.

Our tool combines over 40 databases into one spreadsheet so that your team can see all of the data in front of them instead of manually researching accounts.

For example at your company

\- It looks like your sales team has seen a {{percent change}}% change in the past 3 months.  
\- Your LinkedIn company account has gained {{\# of Followers}} in the past 3 months.  
\- The company looks like it has {{\# of sales people}} people with “Sales” in their title based in the United States today.

Besides things like this, we also monitor for recent news, open job positions, tech on site and mentioned in job descriptions, and a lot more.

On a call, we can build a custom workflow for your team to automate their outbound research. Wanna make it happen?

**Email 4:**

"{{First Name}} – Perhaps this is not your area of focus. Should I potentially reach out to {{Other sales/marketing person in the company that’s NOT them}} given their role as a {{Job title cleaned with AI}}.

**OR**

{{LinkedIn Lead 1}} 

{{LinkedIn Lead 2}}

### Outsourced Software Dev Agency

"""This is how we used Clay to send a fully automated campaign getting responses like this for one of the hardest cold email niches...Outsourced Software Development.

First, I need to start this off by saying that our client on this project is amazing and really gave us space to go nuts on this one. 

Here's how we broke down the campaign. 

1\) We first built a list of founders that have never been founders before OR they don't have technical experience in their past. 

Clay has all of the data you need on this. You can use their AI formula generator to parse the data the way you need. This way, we know we are talking to people who most likely need our help from the beginning. 

We took care of Account targeting in Ocean.io to target software companies. 

2\) We analyzed their main feature pages for what the platform does. Our client has a very particular vertical in software development that he is excellent in. We change the messaging depending on if they have features already that are in his wheelhouse. 

3\) If they have those features, we use an AI model to output ideas on how we could make those features even better. If they don't have those features, we use AI to output what it would look like for them if they did have those features. 

There's some other data points and AI written messaging mixed in but this is the most important part of the campaign. 

4\) we use a final AI integration to just make sure what we are sending isn't too crazy. We can't let generic ideas or off the wall ideas go out to market. 

Then we plug in the custom variables and ship the campaign. 

If you still think sending emails with AI generated content is a waste of time, I would urge you to reconsider. Comment on this post and I can link you to my YouTube channel where we go over campaigns like this all the time."""

### SMB Outreach

Hey {{first name}} \- {{competitor 1}} or {{competitor 2}} seem to be the closest choices customers can choose between from what I can see on Google Maps. 

Are you thinking about ways to make the choice easier for those customers? 

We're helping companies like {{company\_name}} achieve {{outcome}} in {{timeframe}} without {{no good rotten thing}. 

Would this be something you're looking to solve as well? 

**Email 2:** 

I found your phone number {{business phone number, not personal number}} and tried calling but didn't get a response. 

I was about to call {{phone number}} but figured email would be easier

Saw the review about how you {{AI summary of review}}

Looking at your website, the way you stood out in the crowd is X.  

When people are deciding between calling you vs your competitors (get it from yelp) in your immediate area. 

*eg. Be careful about saying anything too bad about the competitors and keep the email language more like healthy competition.*

# **🎲 How To A/B test Value Propositions**  

##  *Phase 1: Test Value Propositions in Batches*

### Why test value propositions? 

Customers often come because they don't know what works. They know I can't wave a magic wand to solve their outbound growth problems, but I can help them experiment fast. 

What we can offer is we can run nine tests in three weeks to see what's working for their audience, handling the 3 main blockers \- (i) Email infrastructure, (ii) Data, (iii) Copywriting. 

We don’t want to guess whether you will succeed. We want to test and validate so we can create a predictable and scalable funnel. 

It is only important to test value propositions. The key thing we're testing is: **DO PEOPLE CARE ABOUT THIS?** 

Same product, just with a different angle. Your prospects might be seeing it that way as well. Try changing the angle at which you present your offering. 

There are so many types of value props that you could talk about. But people care more about certain things. Here’s an example for SalesCraft that we’ve A/B tested. 

**No one cares about:** 

* Email deliverability   
* Copywriting   
* Campaign Strategy 

**Everyone cares about:** 

* Account Scoring   
* Account Enrichment   
* Building list of accounts  
* Disqualifying accounts   
* Contact list building   
* Contact enrichment   
* Contact Scoring   
* Insights and expertise   
* Using AI to personalise at scale 

### Best practices

* Just because someone comes inbound and talks about a certain problem, doesn't mean you'll get the same response when you go out there and talk to strangers via outbound.   
* Pick at least 300 prospects to test your hypothesis via a live campaign. Every industry is different but that's the number we use. That being said, we don't draw even a tiny conclusion until we sent to at least 500 people and I don't draw a full conclusion unless we send to 1000 people. Keep the number consistent. Complete the campaign.   
* Only test one thing. Keep everything else the same.  
  * Do not change copywriting structure or style, only value proposition.   
* Test quickly, before doing any crazy AI personalisations and data workflows. It will save you time and effort building around the correct value proposition.   
* Keep track of the data  
  * Open rate. Must be above 30%, otherwise it’s an email deliverability problem.   
  * Reply rate  
  * Booking rate. 1-3% booking rate is the sweet spot.   
* Focus first on getting email-to-lead ratio as low as possible. Once it’s at its lowest, scale. 

## *Phase 2: When nothing seems to work* 

If you don't get responses, we still have to try to figure out why. In this phase, we lean heavily into different fake domains that we built just for this scenario. We’ll send different angles that are not a sales pitch. We are simply trying to get feedback and learn from them. 

### Type 1: Asking for Honest Feedback As Lead Gen Agency 

"Subject: connection  
Subject: looking for your opinion

Hey, we have a potential client that {{offer/case study outcome sentence}}. 

They told me you'd find it interesting but I wasn't too sure. 

If they could help your {{insert something about the offer}}, would that be useful? 

Signature 

I promise you're not being put in an email sequence so there won't be any follow up. Still if you want me to pound sand, just let me know you're not interested. 

### Type 2: Assume the role of a market research agency 

Essentially, we take on the persona of a market research firm and gauge if people even have the problems or are open to solutions. 

These templates would be sent from domains that point back to a market research company and we basically message about gathering information about what pain points or solutions people need help with right now. 

Subject: your opinion   
Subject: looking for your opinion 

Hey first name, {{Poke the bear question}}. If someone could help {{messaging to be tested}}, would that be useful? 

I promise you're not being put in an email sequence so there won't be any follow up. Still if you want me to pound sand, just let me know you're not interested. 

**OR** 

Request for quote from {{First\_name}}

First name \- we are speaking with other {{leadership type}} leaders and were curious if we could get a quote. 

No call is necessary and we just had 2 questions. 

We asked 50 vp of sales how they could decrease their speed to lead, and these were all their answers. 

* *Question intended to actually ask their opinion about what could be interesting for others in their industry.*

Do you feel like your calendar solution is making things harder to get back to leads faster? How much time on average do you feel your sales rep spend researching a contact in their databases. How many databases go to waste? How many data providers does your sales team have access to? 

* *Questions intended to see if they have a problem you might be able to help solve*

We are looking to share answers from you and your peers anonymously in a report we are gathering together for the market. 

Any response would be appreciated\! 

### 

### Type 3: Assume Persona Of Venture Capital

People love to give their opinion as an expert. We leverage this when we really need answers. 

Subject: would like your opinion   
Subject: trying to learn   
Subject: question for you | investment question 

Hey {{first name}}, we are looking to make a $500k investmnet and we are looking for your opinion. 

The company are we looking at {input filters about target prospects}}. 

{{insert offer/outcome/value/problem to be solved that needs to be tested}}. 

is this something that your team would be looking for? Have you already solved this problem? 

Any advice would be greatly appreciated. We are just trying to do some market research on the company.
